<Author>discerning54
<Content>no night life my first experience of all inclusive in the dominican but went with others who had been on a similar holiday elsewhere.i would class the complex as 4 star, apart from the food, which after a few days became repetetive and was recycled in many forms.the drinks , alcoholic or soft were cheap quality.i would not recommend this resort is you want any action at night. there was insignificant theatrical entertainment for 2 hrs at night,and the only opportunity to dance was in the pitch dark,near the beach with hardly anyone there. the lack of english tourists or opportunities to mix, was a disappointment.there were no facilities for the children, kids activities etc.we were a party of single parents with children from 7- 15yrs. beaches and pools lovely, staff friendly, rooms and service excellent. take plenty of books,as there isn't much else to do, unless you go on the overpriced excursions.Apart from the food the complex itself was a relaxing environment.

<Content>no american speaking staff Was our first fam. vaca allof us 18 and over. First off, rooms refrig/ mini bar was not filled. We had no towels and got into a screaming match with the maids who couldn't understand our problem, then barged in our rooms thinking that we were lying. There is no american tv, you have to pay daily or weekly, also you have to pay for a lock for rooms safe. No one spoke english, the front desk was a disaster. Overall the trip was nice, beautiful ocean, pool area was nice, good buffet when the birds weren't picking at the food. My biggest concern was the lack of staff who couldn't speak or understand us. And the day before our flight out with Delta, they went on strike! but they got that taken care of. I suggest you research all options before booking this resort.

<Author>redsoxfan204
<Content>Buyer Beware My two friends and I staryed at this hotel, but from the first day, we should have seen the sign on the wall. It should have read, no customer service, no flexibility, the rules are the rules and we do no bend to make your stay worth while. First, cleaning the room. Do not expect to have your room cleaned anywhere near the same time each day. 9 am or 6:30 pm. When your room is cleaned, do not expect clean towels until later in the day. Cleaning your room and getting fresh towels in the same visit will not happen. Cleaning staff does not speak any English. Good luck telling them what you want. Good luck in getting extra tells delivered when you call the front desk.Second, using Travelers Checks. They do not cash them for American dollars. They will give you pesos, so you loose money in the exchange. If you bring cash, there is a safe in the room, but it costs per day.Third, the local phone calls are charged at $1.00 per minute. So if you want to call your travel agent, you will pay for the call.We originally requested a folding bed for our visit, but when we got to the room, no such bed was supplied. bottom line: they provide no such amenity. Beds are two doubles or one king, pillows are hard and not flexible. One of us slept on the floor each night. We even asked for a beach chair or mattress, but no luck. Also, each room only gets two keys. So if there are four of you, only 2 keys will be provided.Food was ok for the most part. Not spectacular, but ok. Beach and pook are good. Drinks are also ok. Tours are expensive. they range from $80.00 to $300.00. Golf prices are all over the map with the cheapest being $200.00 with club rental. Tip no included. If I did go back, this is one hotel, I would stay as far away as possible. One more thing, Spirit Airlines is a terrible airline and you will feel like a load of cattle instead of people on a plane

<Author>BigBruno
<Content>Inexpensive Resort/ Poor Food/ Average Accomodations I stayed at the IFA Village from May5-May12 for an inexpensive relaxing getaway. This was my fifth time to the DR and I've stayed at countless other places. I read all of the reviews before I left so I had a good understanding of what to expect. I have a physical disability that limits my walking ability so I figured that this would be a good place to stay since most of the areas are close together.It must not have been busy when I arrived on Monday because I came in after a 25 minute ride on the Apple bus at 11:45AM and though they initially had me farther away from the main area on the third floor(I had requested ground level) they quickly found me another room. I turned around and made three dinner reservations(They even offered for that evening) and I was in my room and unpacked by noon. I spent the $21 for the safe for the peace of mind and it was worth it. The room looked okay when I first entered and it was clean with a King bed that was the hardest bed I ever slept on and I like a firm bed. I had to take Ibuprofen every night so I wouldn't wake up sore in the morning. They had a nice LCD TV in the room which was fine the first 2 days but then they changed their TV and their were no English speaking channels eventhough they had Spanish, French, Italian, German and Chinese. If you wanted to watch TV in English, you had to pay $8 a day for TBS, TNT, Speed and CNN. This was a total ripoff and when I went to complain to the Guest Relations Manager Petra, I encountered the worst person I've ever dealt with in a hotel/resort. She was flat out rude and didn't even want to talk to me. After I wouldn't take thats our new policy for an answer, she started to scream at me. Other than that the room was okay with no view and no patio or balcony. Not many of the rooms have much of a view and none of them have balconies on the Village side. If you want to stay near the main area(main pool, lobby  restaurants, I would stay in the 3000 series of rooms. If you want to be closer to the beach, stay in the 4000. None of them are really beach front. There was no soap in the bathroom so bring your own. On my first day, there were two waters in the refrigerator. I left a $5 tip after the first night and every night thereafter and a note for 4 cervesa's and they put so much Brahma beer, soda and water in my fridge that it was hard to keep everything cold.I ate the first night at the main buffet near the lobby and the food was pretty lame in taste  choices. They tore it down the next day for renovations. I ate at all of the other restaurants as well. The Mexican A'la carte is a buffet and it was pretty weak but the service was good. I've been to other resorts where their appetizer Mexican buffets had more to offer than this did. They did have a great dessert (Chocolate Lasagna) in here. The Asian had pretty decent food with excellent service and the Caribe had the best food and was the most elegant. Other than the pizza buffet by the pool, which was pretty good, the buffets here have really bad food. They lack taste, are cheaper ingredients or are cooked improperly. I would recommend trying to book at the Asian or the Caribe every night. I went back and booked a couple more resevations after my first three and had no problem. In the day time, it's pizza or nothing and pizza gets old after a while. BTW, their coffee and espresso were great!I do enjoy to go to the bars when I'm on vacation and fortunately, I'm really just a beer drinker because the liquor they serve is really sub par. If you want not even top shelf(Absolut, Dewars etc.)it's an extra $7. I was worried about having to drink the Brahma beer instead of Presidente but it turned out to work pretty good because the Brahma was Ice Cold and poured from a bottle instead of a tap. I did find Presidente on tap at the Beach Bar/Disco. The bar service was excellent before I gave them their first tip and they were really good people. Darlin, Juan, Miguel and all of the others gave that nice Dominican Culture to the trip. I usually tipped them $5 at the end of each shift and they treated me like a rock star. The pool area was nice and on the busiest day there, half of the chairs were still empty. The beach was nice and the water too. The beach shuttle was hit and miss on timing and it was hot with no place to sit while waiting for it to come and pick you up at the beach.The IFA Village and Beach Village are average and no more. The Villas are far from everything. The facilities are okay at best. Other than the Guest Relations Manager, the service was very good. This resort is a perfect example of you get what you pay for. I thought I would try to do something on the cheap and get a little more than I expected. It was an okay place to relax by myself for a week but I wouldn't recommend this place to my friends and especially not to anyone with families. I didn't hate it but in hindsight after having to pay the extra money for the safe and TV, I could have stayed at the Iberostar for $100 more.  
<Date>May 23, 2008

<Author>monimaria
<Content>Review of IFA, Bavaro Ocean, Dominican Republic Hello, We are from Montreal (in our early 50s) and we just came back from a 6 days/nights vacation at IFA-Bavaro Ocean (beginning of April-May, 2008).I believe we are advised travelers (Mexico Riviera Maya: Bahia, Palladium, Puerto Vallarta, Cuba: twice, Panama, Costa Rica, Margareta鈥? and we have a good perception of what 4 stars should cost and offer in this type of business. I am writing this note to advice people that this resort is NOT 4 STARS--- except for the rooms. The services are in fact 3 to 31/2 stars. We booked 5 days in advance and this was the only resort available having 3 tennis courts (this was important for us). Who wants to play tennis must avoid this resort. 3 courts are advertised鈥攊n fact are only 2 (plus one basket play ground). The most important thing is the courts are not in the resort; you must walk ~ 10 minutes in the village. The courts are located among private houses of Dominican people; you have to pass in the front of a guard that has a real loaded gun. The courts are not maintained (poor quality surface) have no services at all (no representative from the resort, no water, no bathrooms), dirtiness. We had reservation for each day as requested by the customer service of the hotel. The first day, we arrived on time but the courts were occupied by Dominican people who claimed 鈥渢he courts are their property and if we don鈥檛 like it we have to call the police鈥? We did not comment because there was a possibility that the guy with the gun was paid buy the tennis players. We reported the incident to the hotel customer service and we were assured next day everything will be OK. Next day the courts were available. After one hour play, when we wanted to leave, 3 big dogs showed up at the court door. We manage to get to the hotel, but that was the end of IFA tennis for us. Apart from this, we noticed the people had no training at all in English or not enough training (even at the front desk). They were actually surprised to notice that some people don鈥檛 speak Spanish (amazing !!).   Who likes nightly entertainment/shows must avoid this resort. There is (almost) nothing. NOTHING TO DO AT NIGHT. If it was boring for us, I am wondering what young people should feel like ?! We found the beaches to be gorgeous: fine, white sand, clear water (with algae in places, but this is OK). Too bad they were heavily populated with people offering free presentations of surrounding resorts (very annoying).  Conclusion: This was our first and last 鈥渓ast minute booking鈥? No more IFA for us. We expect a better quality for a 4 stars resort.

<Author>bahiaboundfromont
<Content>2 Great Weeks Of Doing Nothing on arpil 24th my girlfriend and i arrived back home from spending 2 amazing weeks at the Ifa Bavaro Villagei live outside of guelph and my girlfeind is from saskatoon. i parked my vehicle at the econolodge near pearson and went to meet my girl at the airport. we arrived in the DR late that night. the bus trip was very short 15 minutes or so.when we arrived at the Ifa the check in went pretty fast. the sliding door in our first room wouldn't lock so they moved us to another room right away. we then went to the beach disco for a drink and some food { don't eat the rice and chicken balls on the air transat flight, not good }.we have stayed at the 5 star gran bahia pricipe in cancun twice so for a few days we compared the two resorts, there area few things better at the bahia but alot of better things at the ifa. we read many reviews about the ifa and not many of them where good but we knew there was construction going on and it would be pretty much completed before our arrival. we learned from a couple that we met from edmonton that this whole resort has gone through a complete makeover in the past year or so.the food at the ifa was not bad. the pizza bar was amazing, fresh made pizza along with chicken fingers, fries and fresh made burgers oh and yes the ice cream. the buffets didn't change much over the 2 weeks the bacon is deep fried and usually either undercooked or over cooked. we found that the buffet closer to the beach had a better dinner menu. the drink where very strong. they only use small plastic cups so take a big travel cup or mug with you. the drink selection was kind of limited but still pretty good. the beer was nice and cold and mostly poured from a bottle. there are 3 ala cartes, the oriental and the colonial where very very good. the mexican was ok. booked first thing in the morning to get a good seating. the system they have is not very good for booking but you can eat at the ala cartes everynight if you can get a seating. they are not very big.the communication at this resort needs alot of improvement. most try hard, unless you speak spanish or french. to be very honest the people that tried the hardest to communicate where in the restaurants. the front desk staff where really not that helpful in some ways. trying to get a translation from english to spanish can be a chore. we booked with i travel2000.com . we got bumped to later departure and an ealier time to go back home. we flew with airtransat. a little cramped going down but not bad. the food was not good but overall a good flight. the service from nolitours was terrible. no information what so ever all of the binders that had any info where in spanish. we could find and english one till the day we left. when we got to the airport in punta cana our nolitours rep didn't even know what line we had to be in was a joke. the airport in punta cana is pretty cool. the customs and imagration was a breeze to get through but the food and rinks in departures are a huge rip off. $12 for 2 pops and a slice of pizza.to make this a bit shorter i will itimize things and say what we thought about themcommunication - needs alot of improvement but remember we are travelling in a foreign country so we do have to be patientbeach - the beach was amazing, the water was like bath water it was so warm. powdery white sand. many times we just walked for and hour or 2 picking up seashells. it is such a relaxing place to be and if the main resort is too hot you will love the beach always a nice breeze.beach shops - the shop workers will greet you on the beach and bring you into their shops. some can be very persistant but mostly not bad. everyone says they are cheapy cheapy. they love us Canadians. there are not prices on anything. we bought a painting that started at $140 and we got it for $45. never pay what their first price is. offer atleast half if not less. we got an idea of prices from the resort shops and the malls a 15 minute walk away. that will give you a better idea.resort shops - we found the resort shops to be very reasonable price wise with most things. usually you get ripped off at these places but i guess they have alot of competition with the beach shops close by. make sure you bring lots of sunscereen, asprin anything like that these things are very expensive here. internet - there is internet access, $3 dollars for 1/2 hour. if you are from Canada contact your cell phone provider before you go. i could not get service down there with our wonderful bell telephone but pretty much everyone else did no matter what country you are from. we get ripped off by bell and home and away.nightly entertainment - the theatre burned down 2 nights before we got there so all of the night time entertainment was at the beach disco. it was not bad not anything like ths hows at the bahia principe. the beach disco is a pretty cool idea. lost of food drinks music and dancing.rooms - our room was on the second floor right beside the main pool. they have all been redone and they look great. inorder to expand the washrooms the has put the sliding doors on the outer edge of the balcony so no balcony. that was a bit disappointing but didn't ruin our trip. everyday the rooms where cleaned with fresh towels and bed linens. they do not have face cloths so bring them if you need them. no beer or soft drinks in the fridge just water. we took tim hortons coffe along with liquid coffee mate. the coffee in the buffets is very strong and the milk is not very good kinda like carnation milk. after a few days we bought travel mugs so we took our own coffee to breakfast. the rooms where spotless. we saw no bugs but we did get a rain storms one night and the roof leaked so we used the other bed. bring things for the taff there especially the cleaning staff. we took toiletries, socks, veg and flower seeds, pencils, watches things of that nature and also gave a cash tip each day as well.pools - there are 3 pools here. they are not very big but the do look after them pretty good. the main pool is pretty much always busy. there is water arobics there every morning and that is where they have the dance lessons and things. they could have a few more things to do but overall not bad. the other 2 pools are some what deeper and usually not as busy. we went during the slower season so during the busy season they can be very crowded.cafes - there are a few cafes where you can get drinks and very good capicino. make sure you are not wearing a bathing suit in them, you will not get served. shirts are a must here.buffets - pretty much the same menu each day. the selection is not bad a little bit of everything. buffet closer to the beach is the better one especially for dinner.inclosing the ifa bavaro village is a wonderful resort. we all have to remember that we are not at home and we have to be a bit patient when things are not up the the high standards that we have in Canada. there have been some people that have put some very unfair reviews on tripadvisor. some of them are from when we where down there and i don't see how any of the bad things that they say are just. this place is great value for your money. my girlfriend and i are already talking about go back next april. if you are flying out of pearson airport the econolodge is a great place to do the stay and park package. we had 2 weeks parking 1 nights stay when we arrived back and shuttle service as much as we needed back and forth to the airport. it is not a big hotel but they will look after you every well. my contact was a person named ziva and she was very helpful. i booked everything by email juast go too www.choicehotels.ca/cn568please contact me if you have any questions i will be more than happy to help out if i can.brian..

<Author>GnTworldXplorers
<Content>So much for so little! We booked this trip through USA3000 and Apple Tours... Didn't know what to expect and weren't to concerned because the trip was dirt cheap! We were amazed at how beautiful the resort is and it was so big that we discovered that we hadn't even seen the whole place. Our room was next to the swim up bar pool and the pizza restaurant... the pizza was delicious, fresh and available all day! The beach was incredible, beautiful water and lounge chairs for relaxing. If you get to the beach later in the morning then you have to search out lounge chairs. We snorkeled right from a tour out of the resort, it was inexpensive and the site was nice lots of pretty fish. The all-inclusive package was great the food and drinks were all very good, they gave me the dominican rum when I asked for it on the rocks, we also enjoyed the mama juana... the grill by the beach was great and they had a nice assortment of foods to choose from. The buffet restaurant across from the spa is better than the one by the check in desk. It was less crowded and the wait staff was more accommodating. The room was so nice it looked brand new. We had a stocked mini fridge with sprite, coke, beer and water... some of the other guests said they didn't have that. The people that worked at the resort were friendly and we met one of the managers and we were impressed with how much he cared about the resort and the guests having a great time. We met some great Canadian ladies and enjoyed the days on the beach with them :) We walked the beach and there were no shells, I collect them and was shocked that there were none. The sand was pinkish and really clean. Overall we had a wonderful time and would recommend this resort and go back.

<Author>sb8826
<Content>Nice Holiday! Arrived at the IFA Bavaro Village on the 9th in the evening. The check out was quick and everyone was escorted to their rooms-the resort is pitch dark at night time. To my surprise, the rooms were above what i expected. They have been all renovated and are clean, modern and spacious. I have stayed in resorts that claim to be a 5 star rating, but i found these rooms much nicer. The air-conditioning worked very well-infact i was cold most of the time! The fridge was always stocked with bottled water daily, and the cleaning ladies were very friendly.The beach is beautiful. The water is clear and warm-if you are looking for a nice beach get away-this is your destination. There are plenty of chairs on the beach. There isnt a lot of shade, but that didnt seem to bother many. The only thing i found annoying was the party boat that went by every hour with blasting music. Also, there is alot of noise from helicopters and other boats-but after a couple of days, you seem not to notice it anymore. There is a bar and place to eat during the day on the beach, so you can literally spend the whole day there.There are three pools at this resort. The main pool by the village is large, but very noisy and busy. The other two pools are smaller but much more relaxing if that is what you seek.The buffets were ok. There is plenty to choose from but I strongly suggest you book the restaurants in advance for a really enjoyable meal. The Caribe restaurant was delicious. I never made reservations, i just paid the hostess at the door and always got a table. The problem with reservations is that you often get a table late in the evening-often too late to eat.There is a spa on the resort. They give great massages at a good price. You can get a 50 minute massage for 50 dollars. After, you can use the steam room which is very relaxing. They dont tell you this, but once you book a massage-the steam room is free, so take advantage of it-it was great.There is internet on the resort which is the quickest way to communicate to those back home. They charge one dollar-and you can use it for about 20 minutes per visit. I also called collect from the hotel room twice, but the internet is the best way for sure.The only real problem i had with this resort are the prostitutes that are walking around. They sleep and eat at the resort-so you see them in the buffet areas-quite strange. This is a family resort and they shouldnt be there-it was quite sleazy to see them talk to men to try to make deals. I wish management would keep that businness off the resort-especially because Dominican's HIV rate is out of control. I found the staff hardworking and friendly-no issues here. Enjoy your stay at the IFA Bavaro Village-as the week comes to an end...you will wish you had longer!

<Author>cj-sunlovers
<Content>Fabulous Resort First of all, I would like to say that we are not first time travellers. This is our 3rd time in Dominican and we have also been in Cuba. I cannot honestly say anything negative about this resort!! It had it all. There were 3 pools, 3 a la carte restaurants, 2 buffets, pizzeria, beach grill and 7 bars including a swim up bar. The service was fantastic. In certain bars you didn't even have to get up to get your own drink....they would come to you!!! (really liked this feature). There were 2 big markets on each side of the resort and there was deep sea fishing, parasailing, speed boats, catamaran, etc. all right there on the beach.....everything was right at your fingertips.....About half way through our trip, my husband dislocated his shoulder playing beach volleyball!!! and I just had to write about our experience with the health care in this country. It is better than ours!!!!! From the time my husband had the accident, to the time we arrived back our room, we were only gone about 5 hours and we were at the resort for about an hour after the accident. They were very professional, both at the resort and the hospital. We arrived at the hospital in the ambulance about an hour after it happened and he was seen by the doctor right away. The doctor took an x-ray, put him to sleep, put the shoulder back into place, then gave him some good painkilers!!!! The longest part of the stay was waiting for the drugs to wear off and then the doctor put an amazing sling on to support his shoulder. The doctor and most of the staff we dealt with spoke really good english.....we had no problems with communication. We had to pay for the bills, of course, but we do have travel insurance and will be reimbursed 100% for all costs incurred both at the resort and the hospital. A word of advice though.....don't travel without insurance....our bill was $1300.00!!! And you never know when you might need it.Overall, we had an excellent trip. The food was great, as were the drinks. The people were very friendly and spoke very good english. The rooms were superb and kept very clean. I would definately recommend this resort to anyone.

<Author>scapers
<Content>Great Time - Good Deal Left on Feb 28 and home on Mar 6. Wishing that the white stuff falling now was Saona Island sand.Booked trip on a Tuesday and left on Thursday. Great deal. Very good value for your money. We just wanted a fast and cheaper get away and were pleasantly surprised.Beach was awesome. Sufficient lounge chairs and when we couldn't find one, did not hesitate to sit in the sand. One side of the beach is quieter than the other.Room (we were in the 3600 block) was extremely clean. Pleasant and efficient maids. Showers were the best. Always hot water and lots of water pressure. Lighting was no problem. (Last year we brought our own light bulbs). Flatscreen TV with lots to watch. Mattress was hard but we weren't bothered. See Reception for key to wall safe.Meals....average food in the buffet. Always found something we liked. Try the pizza by the pool. We also found an abundance of impatient people. Somehow manners seem to fall to the wayside when food and drinks are involved. Our patience pervailed just the same. Be prepared to rise above.Drinks were plentiful. Only domestic labels. $7 buys you premium brands. We are beer drinkers and loved the Brahma. Poured from bottles. We bought beer from duty free to keep in the hotel fridge. The IFA has 3 pools. One closet to the beach very quiet. The animated pool right outside our door and was tons o' fun. Make a point to find the jacuzzi's. They are located by the villas.Our tour rep failed to tell us about the purchase of phone cards. We learned this last year. Cheap way to call home. Go to the Pharmacy and ask to purchase a card. We paid $4 to talk for 12 minutes. Plenty of time to check in. You can call from your room phone. Just dial 0 and you can get instructions in english.We did the Saona Island day trip. Beautiful is all we can say. We also paid $30 each extra for lobster. Not worth it.Bring your own beach towel if room permits. $20 if you lose hotel towel (and we did!). Thermos for your drinks are also great to bring along. We tipped but doesn't seem to matter. Bring lots of US dollar bills.All in all very pleasantly surprised by the 3.5 star property. Hope this review wasnt too long. Just wanted to share the small things that helped us.

<Author>MissyP3699
<Content>Great! Loved it! First the bad... (but not too much of it, let me say!) No washcloths, language barrier - i speak english only so the spanish was a little difficult! The food was a little different but still not too bad overall. The 3 restaurants they have offer a little more of a formal atmosphere, and they are worth the trouble of making the reservation. Myself and 4 other ladies stayed here and we had all read the mixed reviews of this hotel - we were a little wary of what we would find when we arrived, but we were VERY pleasantly surprised! The rooms were clean, the beds were hard, but the pillows were soft! We stayed in the Ocean section, which is nearest the beach, so no need for any shuttle service to get there. A couple of us were late nighters, but let me tell you, we were in bed by 9:00 pm every night! I guess too much sun in the day! We never made it to the disco and only stayed up for one of the nightly shows! Beware of the roosters that cackle in the early morning hours!!! They got us up bright and early every day....A few tips: Make your reservations for the nice restaurants as soon as you get there - they are open to take reservations from 9:00 to 9:30 each morning. Beware of the mixed drinks - they sneak up on you! Take your own washcloths. If you like Diet Coke, you can only find it in the gift shop or on the beach at the flea market shops - 2.00 Dollars a bottle. Take plenty of sunscreen. Stay at the Ocean or the Village, not the Villas (the Villas appear to be the older section and more like bungalows, but is a really pretty scene there! You would probably need to take a shuttle to the ocean each day...) The Villas section seems to be the most quiet and less inhabited, so if you like that, you might consider it. The Village section (the middle) seems to see the most action and where the water aerobics and swim-up bar is. Fun! Overall, we had a BLAST and we are going to go back next year! Hopefully we can learn a little more Spanish by then.....

<Content>"Pure Paradise" My husband and I stayed at IFA Feb. 2nd - 10th. We are from Shelby Twp. Michigan. This is a #3 star resort. I have to say that out of 5 times to DR now this was our favorite. We have been to 6,5,  4 stars. There was some construction going on up near the Villa's and Cafe'. They are building the most beautiful stone block office and shopping mart. We took a walk everyday to check on the progress and took pictures. How beautiful this is going to be when all done. This did not bother us at all. Why should it? The beds were so comfortable. Light down comforters and big fluffy pillows everything pure white. It was so awesome getting into bed each night. The showers were powerful and huge. The whole room was huge. Coffee pot and full fridge. Miguel is the manager of the buffet and he gave me a liter box of milk for my room everyday after breakfast. I told him I just have to have my milk before bed. He said anything I want or need I can have. No problem. The pools are so clean and beautiful. One more in a shaded area and huge one near the Villa's and another huge one in the Village section. They had big fountain's in them. The whole place was spotless at all times. Even though the help did not speak our english, they knew exactly what I was saying with alittle sign language. Very kind people. The reception area went well. We picked the Ocean section. The food was incredable. Everynight I took alittle of everything, and I husband chose stuck to one thing each individual night; chicken one night, pasta the next, seafood the next, pork the next etc. Thats smart, but I love food and had to have it all. The people raved over the bugers at the beach grill. I ate 3 or 4 each day(without the bun). They were undiscribably delicious. Grilled over a flaming grill. Yes there was chickens running around and peacocks too. Peacocks are serene birds and the chickens had their young trailing behind. NO ONE had a problem with this. Even in the buffet!! It was precious! These people complaining that the cackling in the morning bothered them maybe should not drink so much that their hangover makes them cranky and crotchety. Or if they weren't hung over and complained about the little cackling they are just plain nasty, crabby people. The beach was by far the best along the whole coast. We have stayed up and down the coast. This was like the Blue Lagoon. Huge beach, full of palms. Breathtaking scene. The straw markets on both sides to shop were fun as usual. We took them workers snacks and drinks a couple of days. Had fun sitting and mingling with them. We try to get to know the people there. They are very proud of their heritage and food and everything they do. This bartering we are used to. Its a pleasure to walk through and meet everyone. I chose a 3 star this trip to see the difference. The only difference IS, NO STUCK UP Snobby people walking around making you feel like you have to get off the walk way as they walk towards you! I have come to the conclusion that these kind of UPITY people do not book at a 3 star because they believe that this would not be good enough for them. So better for us normal, smiling, friendly, socialable people that like everyone!! That's how I am looking at it. So that made for a very pleasureable vacation. And for the people that complain about the drinks ; well all I got to say is that if you can't get drunk in Punta Cana then you need 'AA' big time!! Get help!!You are in another country. Tell your self this before going. The food is not going to be like your grandma cooks. Its their culture food. This is their country. YOU are guests! Do not go and come home and pick them apart. This is a beautiful place, something for everyone. I rate it a #10 for sure. For you people out there writing all this nasty stuff and putting down these hard working people, I just hope you find happiness somewhere some day as if you cannot be pleased with IFA and Punta Cana you are very hard to please and don't deserve to be to a blessed wonderful place as this. Stay home. Your sneed remarks are misleading and give other people the totally wrong idea. Thanks to everyone at IFA Bavaro Villa's. I cannot say enough. What a wonderful paradise you are running. Any questions about anything feel free to e-mail-lindaanddon@comcast.net.(From non-judgemental, non-critical, normal people please!!)

<Content>NEGATIVE....... You get what you pay for!!! It was beautiful scenery, but that is all the further it goes. Took 6 hours out of our arrval date to check in, front desk employees does not speak English well enough, and has the worst customer service. Finally received 1 key (only) keying in to our room it was taken by another family. Went to complain and in 5 minutes they had us moved to another room, promising us we would be moved again to be closer to our friends we came with. Never happened the whole week. 2 weeks before arrival we had a confirmed email stating we would have the 3000 block and 3 rooms in a row so we could be all together. Never happened, and yes we requested it once again. Ocean view - Not at all. Quite a walk to the beach. The food was bad. The alcohol was bad. Customer service throughout our resort was bad. There may have been 2 employees that were friendly. We knew people that were moved 4 times due to their air conditioner not working. We had to call about our air also. We had to pay $20 for an extra key so we could keep the air on all day. Once you took your key out of the box for the lights and air it shut off. So your only choice was purchasing a key. After complaing to our Apple Vacation Rep. we got $20 back. We had ants galour. We had to wash everything when we got home. We experience cockroaches, and a mouse. There are no wash rags. Cannot drink the water. It took an hour standing in line to check out, once again it was bad. Our engoyable experience was the excersion we went on (for extra money) and a 10 minute walk to Hard Rock Cafe so we could get some real food and a real beer. It was to die for and the employees there were all about service and happy and cheerful. Our friends never did get their phone fixed after reporting it 5 times. There are no hair dryers in the rooms like they mention. Was great to get back to the states. I know we wil not be back, and do not recommend it.

<Author>isariv007
<Content>IFA Bavaro is Great I travelled to IFA in 2006. I was there is april and july.I work in the travel industry and traveled with a friend who also does. We really enjoyed ourselves. We are both in our 20s.ROOMS: Pretty large compare to other resorts. Very simple but clean. Did have a lezard one time in the room. But it is part of the experience. We were located in the village area. Between the main pool and the smaller one. They do sometimes clean the rooms later in the afternoon. Limited Towels but you can always ask for more.GROUNDS : Amazing. The resort is very big but it is very well kept.There is a short walk to the beach but not that bad. There is a small train making trips to the beach if you dont want to walk.FOOD : The Food was ok. Kinda of repetitive as expected but no major problems. Did not get sick and did not see anyone get sick either. I only ate at the buffet restaurants.BEACH : Amazing beach. Very large and you can swim with no problems. Some activities once or twice a day.POOLS : Did not really hang out at the pool but i know there is activities going on at the main pools during the day.ENTERTAINMENT : There are shows everynight. Dance, and comedy wich requires participation. I found them amusing and funny. You just need an open mind and people willing to let loose a bit.DISCO : Never crowded but it was still really fun. The disco is on the beach which is really cool. Variety of music : Salsa, Hip hop, Dance etc. You can also make requests. There is a bigger disco in the another resort 10-15 mins from the hotel if you feel like partying all night. STAFF : Very friendly, We got a great service, Sometimes had to wait in line at some bars but not for long. OVERALL : Great Resort for everyone. The crowd was mixed. Families , couples, young singles ... A lot of Europeans. Good choice and it is one of the less expensive resorts in punta cana.If you have questions, do not hesitate.

<Content>Negative Reviews!!!!!!! Are There 2 Ifa"S we just returned from ifa village resort on feb 7....i have to say after reading all the negative reviews over the last weeks prior ,i wondered what we have done..Let me say now ANYONE thinking as i did NEED NOT WORRY....we stayed in room 3419 close to center pool and pizza house/bar...the room was above expectations ,clean,no mold(as others mentioned)and all worked.We always had excellant water pressure and hot water..we asked for king size bed but got 2 doubles and lived with it because the room was so nice,,,as others reviews have mentioned the beds were hard but they are the same everywhere i have been when travelling south...certainly NOT unsleepable....i would get up everymorning to look out and see the grounds being cleaned... THIS PLACE WAS NICE....there were 2 buildings being revamped closest to the ocean(the maids were in 1 setting up when we left) but it certainly was not a problem for us..As for the beach, i dont think anybody in their right mind can complain...the beach market venders can be intimidating but i can deal with them(never paid more than 50% of their asking price/offer less then walk away they will call you back) The staff::: were all nice however hard to communicate with but not impossible...we had no problem with maid service in our room at all,,,if they ran out of towels while doing rooms they brought them later(2 times) one time still warm The bars;;i used them all.....all excellant The food;;all i can say is dominican food...being a select eater i would have liked to see roast beef everynight...but their was always a selection to try and i never went hungry...the pizza at the pizzaria was excellant...you have to try to hot/spicy one(halapienio peppers??) because you need a drink chaser to cool your mouth, we tried the caribe alacarte the filet mignon was excellant,,i spoke with others who tried the japanese restaurant who said was good...the breakfasts were good(the usual setups,stand in line for egg selections or buffet french toast,pancakes,yogurt,breads etc) I spent time with friends at 2 other resorts while down there,they said same food selections as ifa We cabbed it to one resort 16.00US for a twenty minute trip and a driver(nicolas) who spoke english...He told me if the cabbie wasnt wearing a pink shirt he was not a legite cabbie be careful We didnt make it to the live shows or the disco...i have seen them at other resorts they are all the same ,we brought our own wine and whiskey down so elected to spend time in room at night and relax...which was quiet (as others had complained about) The pools consisted of 3..the center was the busiest the other 2 were were more quiet(never went only passed by).the walk to beach form our area was 5 minutes and quite relaxing,they are doing some ground restucturing from ocean buildings to beach(certainly not disrupting) To sum up this review i feel this was an excellant resort for the money we spent....its what you make of your vacation  Please if anyone wants to email me with questions feel free wilkinsauto@rogers.com

<Rating>4	4	4	4	5	3	4	5

<Author>Marval
<Content>IFA Bavaro needs to get their act together! Three of us went (booked two rooms) January 10 - 17, 2008. Needed to get away from the winter and cold, wanted a reasonably priced trip, and also a trip that could fit into our schedules in terms of dates.I had read a number of reviews, so tried to keep a pretty open mind., having been to AI's in Cuba and Mexico. This trip was booked through Signature Vacations in Canada which is a fairly reputable company, but clearly, they need to check on amenities before they post them in their brochures.For example, the brochure stated the rooms had ceiling fans, full bathrooms (which means including a bathtub) and all rooms have balconies and terraces. All of the foregoing was not true.Because one of the members in my party has some mobility issues, I requested we be located close to the main reception area and restaurant. I can say that surprisingly, those requests were addressed upon check in.We didn't have any problems at check-in per se, except we felt that the communication skills by most of the front desk people were sadly lacking. My primary language is English, with some French and a bit of Spanish, but it was next to impossible. There is nothing to make you feel welcome, nor does there appear to be any commitment to customer service or making a guest happy. More of that later. The lobby really needs some improvement. There isn't a clock, there are no notices up showing anything, and just no communication or information. It would have been very helpful if information was posted on shuttles, busses, excursions, etc. This would have helped enormously and saved a lot of time and effort in trying to figure this all out and constantly be asking and hoping you are receiving the correct information.Nornally, you will see something up that shows the entertainment and that kind of thing. We had no idea there was a 2 hour time difference, but I figured it out my first morning - my clock said 6:30 a.m., but everything was already bustling and people were sitting at the pool and already eating breakfast.We were in the hotel section facing the large pool and very close to the main restaurant. So that was OK. What was silly, is they only provide you with one key card per room. so even though 2 were sharing one room, they would not budge on this, which makes it difficult if people want to do their own thing. The rooms disappointingly had no balconies or terraces, which means you could not enjoy an early morning coffee or sit outside at night unless you left your room. As well, no ceiling fans and only a shower stall. The rooms were clean and the maids were decent. We did find it strange that neither kleenex or small bottles of body lotion are provided. The showers have a dispenser with soap, shampoo and conditioner, and a little dish of wrapped typical hotel soaps are placed by the sink, and that is it.The other issue - constant blaring music. I enjoy some good music, but not to the point where I am constantly being assaulted and having to listen to these animators continuously yappying on a microphone. I am not trying to be intolerant, but I really want to be able to chill and relax. Luckily, we found another very large and nice pool where the nightly entertainment is held, which suited us beautifully. Very relaxing and quiet. The service at the bar at that pool (I think it was called Margarita's) was very good and the bartender was very polite. I am not a big drinker, but enjoyed the CocoLoco's - otherwise I drank soda water with lime. I used an insulated mug which is the way to go - you get a decent amount to drink and it stays cold. The so called diet coke was awful, and I think it was a local cola.I had problems with my cable, took 2 days for them to address it - I can't tell you how many times I must have reported it. They have a couple of people working at guest services who are rude and snarky. I think when I finally said I would take this further, I coerced someone into action, as the girl then sweetly told me she made a special call on my behalf and had it fixed. There is one blonde girl who is very good at guest services, and she speaks excellent English, but she wasn't always there. So more often than not, I had to deal with the other two, who really need to have some training.I don't mind a hard bed, but this was beyond hard. It was like lying on a slab of concrete and the pillows were lumpy and strange. It also took me 2 days and many requests to land a couple of extra pillows.The beach itself was absolutely stunning. You can either take a shuttle which stops regularly in front of the main lobby or walk. It isn't a bad walk, but this place really isn't what I call beachfront.Again, the music would blare with the silly announcements at the beach, but we would just move away and were able to get a bit of peace. There is a snack bar there which is for the guests of the resort which had hamburgers, hot dogs, french fries, some salad, fruit, crepes, etc., so you won't starve. It was OK, especially when you don't want to trapise back to the hotel for lunch. There are a couple of markets, but they really descend on you and bug you if you are looking around. I didn't see much to buy, but purchased a couple of small packs of coffee and a pair of earrings. The first time I went they quoted me 8 dollars for the earrings. I went back and they then quoted me 25 dollars for the same earrings, I paid 5 which I think was a fair price.The other thing that bothered us was there were only beach loungers, no chairs. I don't mind loungers to a point, but can't sit in one all day. And one of my travelling companions definitely can't use one at all - so at the pool I would drag a chair to the pool from the seating area for the entertainment, and I would bring a chair down from the snack bar for the beach. It is a pity that guest comfort is not a consideration.There is also a pizza snack bar by the main pool which serves pretty OK pizza, drinks, french fries, etc. It is a pleasant area to sit for awhile, but during the afternoon you will once again be bombarded by loud, blaring music. We would sometimes go there at night after dinner to sit, as at least it was quiet at that point, and we didn't want to be stuck in our rooms, because again, no balcony or terrace.The other thing that struck us - much of the main area and paths are made of this type of cobblestone. The maids and workers would dutifully scrub this area every morning, and I saw one older woman take quite a tumble as it was always wet early in the morning, so take caution. As well, any time any one was wheeling a cart or their luggage, it made the worst racket. Not a very good design feature.The food was so-so. Some strange items I wouldn't touch, but you won't go hungry. I would usually have yoghurt, lots of great fresh fruit and there were decent buns and breads, croissants, etc. The toaster didn't work worth a da**, so not worth using. They would often run out of things like glasses, spoons, butter, etc., so you had to keep bugging staff for that. The staff working in the main restaurant were quite hard working and for the most part, very good. We would sit in the non smoking and had a couple of very good people that would look after us. I tipped them a couple of times, because they really do work hard.Although we sat in non-smoking, there was still an awful lot of smoking going on all over the place and I saw a lot of pregnant European women smoking and it really bugged me, but different attitudes and outlook I suppose.Dinners were a bit of another story. What saved me was an OK pasta bar, and I ended up eating that three times and it was acceptable, because at least you could pick and choose what items you wanted. The fresh vegetables were good, and there were some good items on the sweet table.We went to two of the specialty restaurants. When you make reservations they always tell you how booked these places are, but in reality, there are very few people. The Japanese one was a waste of time. Very lovely setting, but the service was lousy and they botched up my order - I ordered the shrimp and vegetable noodle dish but there were no shrimps. I explained there was no cameron (Shrimp in Spanish) and they kept telling me I didn't want shrimp. Oh brother.The Mexican restaurant was OK - the guacamole was certainly not as I expected, but it was edible and the chicken taco was good. It is also buffet style, you only get served your drink and dessert. I had ice cream because I had been craving it and the main restaurant doesn't serve it, which is a pity.There is also a lounge/coffee place called Dominico's which is quite pleasant, and we went there after dinner to sit for awhile. The coffee in DR is fantastic, but they freaked when I ordered an iced coffee. I ended up going to the bar and explaining what I wanted, they looked at me as though I was crazy. Oh well. The service was at times very slow here and there wasn't enough seating, it seemed to be a popular spot.Luckily, the weather was fantastic, which saved the trip - otherwise, we would have probably gone out of our minds. I guess lesson learned. The brochure listed this property as a 4 star, but it isn't. I doubt I would return to this property, unless they made some improvements - such as decent help in the main area, better communications, and balconies!I always meet people and make some long lasting acquaintances from my many trips, and this is the first time I wasn't able to speak to anyone outside of hotel staff. I enjoy a multi-cultural environment, but no one outside of our party of three seemed to speak English, so it was kind of disappointing.I would come back to Punta Cana, but would pay a bit more to stay in a superior property.

<Author>H_Brock
<Content>AMAZING, Absolutely Brilliant! We stayed here last week (Jan 7-14). Had a great time! The food was excellent, our room was well kempt, the employees are nice, the beach is spectacular and the pool more-so. I have read some of these reviews and alot changed about the resort even whilst we were staying there. IFA is trying very hard to make this resort a 5-Star hotel by spring break. For example when we arrived a building was just having the walls put up and by the time we left, windows, tiles, flooring etc had already been completed. There is a fair bit of construction occouring as walk between your rooms and the beach however it hardly bother us to be honest. The spa is excellent as well and the food at the a le carte's were spectacular with great service and atmosphere (eat at the Caribe, the filet mignon was brilliant). We personally had no problems with our room, however one of the people we met down there had their roof eak when it rained however reception quickly gave them a new room and were on the roof of our building the next day. The disco was shite to be honest as the DJ's would play loud latin music for the first hour but after that it was a pretty fun time with more western music so long as you keep the liquor flowing. Food I would give a four out of five and I would personally say this is one of the best resorts I have been to. Be wary of what is written on here that is over two weeks old because, like i said, the resort is changing quickly to bring forward a fresh face for spring break.P.S. Try a tequila boom boom. Wont feel the alcohol, but it will hit you 10 minutes later, and the local drink mahiuana.As well, at the Cafe Dominicano ask for Mary mercedes, she was the best waiter I have ever had. Tipped her $10 at the end of our trip.

<Author>Kate099
<Content>Don't go! Don't Go! We booked eight weeks in advance and paid $1, 500 a piece - from Dec 30 - Jan 6 / 08. We booked to stay in the IFA Bravero Villages, but when we arrived, they put us up in the Villas(3 star vs. 4 star villages) The Villas are set back a far distance from the lobby and main pool area - there was a trolly taking people to and from, but seemed to be full or not operational all the time... Our flight was late and we checked in late, we realized the mistake when we reached our rooms. The six of us (all couples) had many problems with our rooms: 1 had no a/c, another no tv, and in ours the bedding was questionably dirty - my main problem was the long walk to and from the pool (15 min. and another 15 to the beach). We complained about our problems and were moved 2 days later to a building in the Villages - a new building still being worked on. Here we had no hotwater and no tv as they were not hooked up yet. After complaining again, 2 days later, we moved to the inner Villages - our third move-in...ahhhhhhhhh Here, the rooms were descent, but our room still had no tv! Which was a drag as it rained two days straight... It seems as though we spent a lot of our valubale vacation time at the front desk bitching and complaining about the accomodations than we did enjoying ourselves. The hotel was under construction and there was heavy machinery and work crews everywhere! Banging, drilling, jackhammering going on daily!THe Food - ok. a lot of weird and unusual dishes though - we banked on the omelettes in the morning and the pizzeria - AWESOME!... AVOID the a la carte restaurants - one was a buffet (much the same as the main restaurant) the other two were not the most tasty or reliable. Beach - Ok. the water was a nice colour of blue and green, but fairly merky and cool. A lot of seaweed washing up to shore. Most days chairs were available on the beach and around the pool.Locals / Help / Management - the workers were fairly nice and would smile and dance and be happy to see you....The management and help were LESS than helpful or accomodating - truly a disapointment! The magager was however, fairly reasonable and tried to help us after waiting to see him for many hours every time. Pool  Drinks - a large pool ajoined to a pool bar - both were good. Drinks were made differently at every bar and the slushly type drinks were never really slushy consistenly...:(Entertainment - not a lot. There was a kids daycare and activites for them though...OVERALL: We are accepting nothing less than a full or partial refund or travel voucher - we are all so displeased with this resort... We were stressed out and not ourselves the whole week (other then the last day when all was finally going well...) Please don't waist the money here avoid IFA at all costs. We are reasonable people and can put up with some things, but all mentioned above was way too much!Hope this helps.Kate :)

No IFA in our future - sorry...but I can't even believe that they would rent rooms. Our visit was meant to be a relaxing Thanksgiving vacation - not a nightmare!!

<Author>Manchester_Legend
<Content>Lovers Paradise We stayed 1st to 8th October 2007 and had a wonderful time. WEATHER: Mixed, sunny early and late hours but rain (sometimes very heavy) during daytimes. It was cloudy but still very hot and we still got sunburned! The clouds suited us as we are fair skinned so this was a godsend. There is little shelter on the beach or around the pool areas.HOTEL: On arrival we were faced with building/refurbishment work on the village side of the complex.However, this did not in any way spoil our stay there, there was no machinary noise and the area was fenced off.The room was clean and spacious with two double beds and a large balcony. We stopped in the Ocean village part of the complex which nearest the beach, this was a big plus. The only downside was the shower which needs upgrading.Throuhout the grounds of the hotel there are motorised buggies that ferry you around the complex. The swimming pools are clean and relaxing. One has a bar serving cocktails etc all day. One pool was closed due to the refurbishment. However, when this is complete it will be fantastic.FOOD: Was always good with plenty of choice for young and old.You must try the 3 a la carte restaurants which offer a special service especially suitable for couples (not kids).STAFF: They were very friendly, courtious and attentive. Never an empty glass or dirty plate in sight and couldnt do enough for you.TIPS: Hotel policy at this all inclusive hotel is not to tip but the service was so good that we did sneak them a tip.BEACH: White sandy beach with clear blue sea with safe swimming zones and water sports.OVERALL: We had a great time and would suggest this is a holiday for couples who want a relaxing beach holiday.

<Author>mlesagonicz
<Content>Great vacation for the money Just arrived home yesterday from Ifa Bavaro Village. We traveled with another couple, and a total of four teenage girls, from 14 to 17 years old. We had a vey fun time, but the day was never long enough to just relax. At the beach they offered catamarans, and if you didn't know how to steer it, you could ask for a driver, which we did, and just tipped him. He took three of the girls out all along the coast, stayed out for an entire hour, and even jumped off the catamaran to pick up a huge star fish for them to look at. the beach was pretty, we always found palm trees to sit under, as after the first day, we needed the shade. Plenty of chairs, the water was always calm, and the sand was cool.Their was a language barrier with the employees and the other guests, but with my very little spanish language, we got by just fine, and we all had a great time trying to interpret each other. We used alot of sign language, but came away with a lot of great laughs, and great memories. We tipped often, only because the people worked so hard, and I know they truly appreciated the tips. The manager at the buffet came to our table every night a few times making sure eveything was fine. The food was very good, with alot of variety for dinner at the buffet by the pool. Try the different foods, and you will be pleasently surprised. Abundant with fresh, sweet fruit, smoothies, and lots of alcoholic drinks. The room was OK, but clean. No wash cloths, we had to ask for extra towels the first day, but after that, we never had to ask again. By the second day, they filled our refrigerator with beer, soda, and water. The beds were hard, but we were so exhausted by the time we made it to bed, I still slept like a baby. The entertainment crew worked really hard, and they seemed to have a difficult time getting people to get involved, but when they did, they had a good time. The nightly entertainment wasn't at all what I expected, but we went every night to the disco, and got some laughs out of it. I recommend making reservations at the Mexican  Japanese Rest. The food was wonderful, and so was the atmosphere. They are doing construction, and I would like to see it in about another two years, it looks like it will be beautiful. We had a great time, you can always find something to coomplain about, but we went to have a good time, and we did. For the money, this was a nice place to go, and I am glad we did.  
<Date>Jul 29, 2007

<Content>Could be better I have stayed in this hotel for a week with my boyfriend. I can't say that I was very disapointed, but I wasn't very happy about the trip too. It is, probably, because I have stayed at 5 star hotels before. My biggest complain will be the SERVICE:Non of the staff spoke english, and most of them were rude and unhappy. Many times barteneders ignored us, but it wasn't busy. If I have tried to ask for something, they did not even try to understand me. I have been drinking beer and wine for the whole week, because the cocktails were awful. Once I have asked for baileys, and they said I should pay $5.00 for that. I'm not cheap, but isn't it suppose to be all inclusive?Another thing I didn't like was the meal times. There were to big spaces between the meals. Sometimes we were hungry and had to wait until they start servig lunch or dinner. Both me and my boyfriend usually going to bed very late, and we wake up very late. If we woke up after 10:30pm we had to be hungry until lunch (which is I think is at 1:00pm or 2:00pm). But we didn't want to wake up at 8:00 or 9:00pm on our vacation and be tired all day.The FOOD was ok. Liked the a la carte restauants, especially Japanese one. Didn't like Mexican, because it seemed to us like a regular taco bell. The buffets were ok, but not too much variety. Especially the beach one, which was opened for lunch. I was hoping to get some nicely cooked meat or seafood, well they had a bit of that, so I wasn't hungry.The ROOMS are nice and clean, but nothing special. We tipped the maid daily, but she never did any towel swans etc., which they always do in other hotels. On one day, lots of ants suddenly appeared in our bathroom. It looked like somebody spilled something sweet on the floor, and ants have covered this small area. But we have never eaten or drunk something other than water in our room. It was late night, so we were too lazy to go to the reception. So we just killed them using my perfume and hairspray. The bathroon was cleaned the next day by maid. The BEACH was great. Can't somplain about that. Nice warm water, sand and tall palm trees. We spend most of our day there, so I cannot say anything about the pool.ENTERTAIMENT was ok. Lots of activities during the day, but we didn't like the evening shows, because they were mostly in Spanish. Disco on the beach was good, but they play lots of latin music, which most people (not me) didn't like, and sometimes disco was pretty quite.Overall, if you have never been to more expensive resort you will like this place. If you looking for something more luxury, pay extra 200-300 dollars and go to a better place, which I will do next time.

<Author>kelsytropico
<Content>Great Little Hotel We stay at the IFA Ocean Village the 3rd week of March, I must admit we have a fanastic time. It is not 5star, but good value with nice amentities. The room was sparkling clean, had 20 foot vaulted ceilings, a beautiful view of the AMAZING ocean, a TV with lots of stations, Bathroom with all the neccesities, decent enough bed  pillows. After reading the reviews, we were worried about the room...I even brought scented candles and our own pillows....but we never had a thing to worry about. Room was perfect.The pools were great, warm and clean. Never had a problem getting a chair by the pools. The beach was AWESOME. We coudn't say enough good things about it. Very clean. Had to be there before 10am to get a good chair, but the couple of mornings we slept in, we were stil able to find a decent spot. The grounds were beautiful, we loved waking around and trying new pools and new bars.Food was good. I don't plan on trying every single thing every day, so by eating like a normal person, I never got sick of the food. The pasta one night, soup  salad the next...that sort of thing...eating normal amounts. The soups, although a strange green colour were fabulous. We were able to try all the restaurants and found them all good. Not amazing, knock your socks off, but I was always full and happy. Best things were the pasta grill, omelet station, fresh veggies/fruit, the meat of the day, ice cream. The a l'cartes were good. Great service and they felt like you were in a nice resturaunt. I really liked lunch: the beach buffet was awesome (crepes, chicken, fresh salad and fruit....). and the pool bar had some of the BEST pizza i have ever had. Drinks were soooo strong. I am talking almost all rum. I sometimes asked for a extra coke. They have great bar menus with lots of new drinks to try. Every bar tender was very different, so depending on who was serving you the drink recipe could change. I liked it. Kept it interesting.The entertainment staff was funny....they mostly hit on single girls and played the same song over and over. But I did do some beach aerboics and it was fun. Played bingo...didn't do the shows or the disco. We mostly just had drinks at night and fell asleep early to a movie on TBS.Service was always good, check-in/check-out a breeze, no problems with reservations, everything went as it should. We tipped a little bit, tried to speak spanish, and followed the golden rule. It is so frustrating to hear people complain about the staff not speaking english, you are in THEIR country. Stop being so closed-minded, Things are different in a DIFFERENT country. Food will not be the same. Service will be different. Nothing was bad ever, sometimes things were different though. If you can't accept that you might as well go to a resort where it is completely north-americanized, not this small resort with alot of character and charm. I am not new at all-inclusives, I have been to many 3,4,5 star places. This placed is great for 3.5stars, it was more than i was expecting and I would go back for a simple, but nice, holiday.

<Author>Idahothoughts
<Content>Once was enough! The purspose of the trip was for my sisters and I to take our mother on her first all inclusive trip and be together for the first time without our spouses or brothers. A girl trip. My sister booked the trip for us..she had been there quite a few years earlier with friends and had enjoyed herself. Many things had changed since her last visit (way less free activities).I had never been on a trip where the main language spoken was not English or French. I went with no Spanish and that was a mistake. By the end of the week I had learned quite a bit and that helped make things better. Bring your pocket dictionnary if you do not speak the language.Since returning I have read the reviews and I have to say that they are all pretty acurate. The good, the bad and the ugly. The reception people upon arrival were rude and un-friendly...They tried putting us in a very very smoky room, that was nasty. They finally agreed after they attempted to clean it and a night spent in it that it was as bad as we said. Had to pay $21 for use of the safe.The rooms were old, fridges were rusty, the pillows lumpy...Our room and maids did a tremendous job in keeping the room clean. They were constantly mopping the hallways. They were very slow at getting clean towels to the room, sometimes it was after 5PM. The beach towels were always in abundance for towel exchange though. Sometimes we traded our dirly beach towel for a clean one to shower with. The hot water was out more than it was on..however cold water is not very cold there. Our electricity did go out during the night for a few hours. The fan and AC were noisy. The water in the tank of both toilets (two rooms) never shut off, no mater how many times you worked the tank. The rooms facing the main pool are noisy all day long due to the live entertainment but it was also fun to sit there and watch the activity around the pool. Pool chairs must be claimed by 7:30 AM or you are out of luck for the whole day. Most people put their towels on them before breakfast. Beach chairs with shade had to be claimed by that time too. Long walk to the beach or a bus ride and you still have to walk. No waves due to coral reef way out. Swim area surrounded by rope and noisy boats and smelly boat fuel. Water was crystal clear, the bottom of the ocean was either beautiful white sand or short weeds. Lots of floating weed debri and beach edge wasn't ever raked up while we were there.Beach is long, white with beautiful sand and Palm trees.The gounds are beautifully kept. Always someone cleaning up.The food..It was good the first 3 days until you tasted everything and realised it was just OK. Fruit was always good though. My family enjoyed the coffee bar at night. Surprisingly there was very little fish to be enjoyedThe Mexican was good, do not expect the American version of it though...Japanese was closed and the Colonial was ok too. You need to reserve a few days before to get a spot and it is worth it just to get out of the crowded rude people at the buffets. Many Europeans were so pushy about getting their food, they would just jump in front of you like the food was going to disappear.You could order the same drink 10 times from the same waiter and it would never be the same. Their orange juice was more like Tang, yuck. All their drinks were so watered down, the only way to get drunk on the free drinks was if you asked them for an extra shot. Good luck at getting them to understand that.The entertaiment was sometimes fantastic, sometimes crude and sometimes just long and boring. The same 16 people did all the shows, entertainment around the pool, exercise and games. They were quite a few talented dancers...Very hard workers.I was not happy when I first arrived, no one tried to speak English even though we attempted Spanish, after a few tips some of the waiters warmed up to us. I told the gentelmean in charge of service that his employees needed name tags and to smile more..he agreed and he said they were workng on the name tags. I think it is important to recognise the employees who excel at their jobs and make you feel like you are on vacation. So many employees made me feel like I was imposing on them.The only free stuff to do was renting the mini sail boats and kayaks and you neededa $30 deposit to do that.The half day shark and sting ray excursion  was fun but a little expensive ($78 US). After I got over what I did not like and could not change about this place I started enjoying myself. I was there for relaxation, sunshine, being with my family, long walks and I got to do all that.I think I got what I paid for... but next time I would pay more and hopefully get more.I don't see myself going back there...not enough Americans... each resort on both sides of this one had tons of Americans on the beach. One way to tell was by their Quicksilver and Biilabong bathing suits, IFA had too many Speedos and topless women who should have kept the girls hidden (sorry ladies...).

<Author>sam81
<Content>Good and bad My boyfriend and I stayed at IFA from Feb 7th to the 14th. We had a nice trip but there are definitly some things about this resort that need improvement.Rooms: The resort is broken up into three sections. The farthest one from the beach is the villa section, the middle section is the village and the one closest to the beach is the ocean section. When we first arrived at the resort, we were in the ocean section. If you are planning on staying here, make sure you put in a request with your agency to stay in the village part of the resort. Our first impression of the room was aweful. The super 8 has nicer rooms. We were on the first floor (i had requested 2nd or 3rd) and we had two double beds instead of a king size. My boyfriend and I are both really tall and we sleep in a queen size bed at home, so we really didn't want to be spending our vacation squished into a tiny bed. The air conditioning barely worked and it was so humid in the room that the beds felt wet. The view from our patio was the path that goes to the beach and if we had the curtains open we had people staring right into our room. There was also a security guard right outside 24/7. One day we opened the door and he was leaning up against our balcony. There was also what looked like a big pile of garbage outside. Not a very nice view. The bathroom was not what you'd expect to find at any all inclusive resort. It was horrible and old. We had read lots of review complaining about the rooms before we came and one by one all the things we read about were coming true....light switches that do nothing, a broken patio door (it came right off the railing and wouldn't close and they said they'd fix it and never did), no hot water, the disco being loud, etc. Some reviews mention low lighting....this is because the lamps that they use (at least in the ocean section) have energy saving bulbs in them and they give off a different colour of light. Instead of a nice evening glow you get a sort of sci-fi look. Not very romantic. Anyways, the next day we asked to be moved to a room with a king size bed and we were told that we'd be able to move the next day at 2:00. We were put in the village section on the second floor with a beautiful view of the main pool. This room was a MILLION times better than the other one. I can't even believe they were in the same hotel. There were swan shaped towels on our bed (king size bed!) and little red flowers everywhere. The airconditioning worked really well and the bathroom was newer and nicer than the other one (not as nice at a 4 or 5 star but still decent). We were much happier in this room...the only complaint I would have is that we could smell cigarette smoke that I believe was coming in through the air conditioning. Gross!. Also, they only give you water in your fridge....I knew there wouldn't be alcohol but I thought there would at least be some pop. My boyfriend at I went to the mini market one day to buy a couple bags of chips and a two litre of pepsi for the room and it came to $16 american!! I would strongly suggest buying a bottle of duty free on the plane to have in your room and bringing pop with you or snacks in your suitcase. On our last day, our flight home was 7 hours late so we ended up staying at the resort and swimming all day. Because we had already checked out of our room, they gave us a courtasy room to shower in before going to the airport. The room was in the villas section so it gave us the opportunity to see what they were like. This room was almost worse than the first. It looked so run down, again I can't believe it's part of the same hotel. If you go here, make sure you stay in the village!Food: The food here is great! The buffet breakfast is really really good...amazing omlettes and pretty much everything else you can think of. Crispy bacon! It's hard not to go all out on breakfast! The grill by the beach is good...hamburgers and hot dogs (although the ketchup tastes like apple cider vinigar...so does the mayo and pretty much every other kind of sauce!). They also have delicious chicken wings and fries and crepes! I waited til the last day to have a crepe and I wish I had tried them sooner. There is a pizzeria by the main pool and I swear it's the best pizza in the world. I was so sad to leave it. The mexican restaurant is really good and the japanese is just ok. The buffet at night is great....always something for everyone. We didn't try the caribe.Beach: AMAZING!!! But if you like waves, there is a reef at this section of the beach so there are none. But it's still paradise!Pools: We only swam in the main pool in the village section and it's very nice. There is a small pool in the ocean section that looks nice and a bigger one in the villas section...also really nice. There is no bar tender for the swim up bar. So if you want a resort with a swim up bar, don't stay here! Disapointing. Also, if you want alcohol in your banana mama or your pina colada, you have to ask for it. I was drinking virgins for the first day and a half!Show: AWESOME AWESOME AWESOME!! If you're a so you think you can dance fan like I am then you'll love the show. I don't know where they get these dancers from but they're amazing! And all the girls are beautiful!Animation: They animation staff are really good...always doing something. There's a group by the main pool and a group by the beach. They do things like morning stretching, arobics, dance lessons and crazy games in the afternoon. The only annoying thing is that you'll here the same 4 or 5 songs over and over and over again! (Latinos!!)Disco: The disco is ok....punta cana is really relaxed and there's not much of a night life. My bf and i were too tired most of the time anyways. It would probably be more fun if you went with a group of people.Service: The service was good except for the front desk staff which I found to be a bit rude. All in all I think this is a nice resort if you're not picky about details. I didn't think that I was, but after this trip I'm afraid I'm turing into a bit of a snob! If you've ever stayed at a 5 star before then you'll probably be dissapointed. Go there with a positive attitude, switch rooms if you have to and everything else should be fine. Oh yah...don't go to the palma real shopping mall....it's not finished yet and the bus leaves you there for at least two hours. We wanted to go back after 40 minutes and were kinda stranded! If you have any questions about this resort you can e-mail me.... samanthanne81@hotmail.com
