<Author>eez247
<Content>Great! I will post this review under both the IFA Villas and IFA Village as they are part of the same resort complex.Overall this resort is above average and I would rate it a four out of five.My girlfreind and I (both 27) arrive on JAn 29 and stayed until Feb 5, 2007.Facilities:Upon arrival they put us in the Villas section, room 1089, I asked them if they could move us closer to the beach and they said they would have a room in the 4000 block on the 31st.THe VIllas section is quite a ways away from the beach. The higher your room number in the 1000 block the further away you are. Overall my room in the Villas section was a little run down compared to the room I was given later in the 4000 block. I the worst problems were the shower( no tub) was very low flow and took a long time for the water to turn hot. Also the refrigerator did not seem to cool very well even on high. The TV had no remote and the front door did not seem very secure. I would recommend everyone to rent a safe ( $3 dollars a day) The Villas overall wuold be good for someone who would prefere a quiet location pool site rather then a crowded beach. Or the foot traffic of the other more central pools.The main stage, 3 al cart restaurant , a pool bar and Captain lounge are all located in the Villas section. The 2 buffet restaurants are located in the other parts of the complex so they are bit of a walk to get to.On the January 31 we moved to our room in the 4000 block in the Oceans Village section (4036). The room overall was in much better shape the our other room in the Villas The biigest improvement was the flow of the shower. The TV had a remote and as we were on the third flow we had a balcony. We were now only a short walk from the beach.The beach was great but make sure you wake up early and put a towel on a chair. Many days we slept in and could not find an empty chair and had to go over the Barcelo section of beach.Find the stage and stay away from it if you prefer quite as they like to blast the music.I found the grounds were very well kept and secureFoodOverall the food was very good. You could aways get something to eat from 7 Am to 3AM. The buffets offer an abundance of different foods. They always have someone on the grill cooking something. My personal favorite was breakfast, the cook woould prepare an omelette for you from an assortment of ingredients for your selection. My only complaint would be that sometime the waiter or waitress would take too long to get my drink and I'd be finished eating by the time it arrived. I only ate at the International a la carte restaurant so I can not comment on the other two. Many days I would grab a slice of pizza from the snack bar beside the pool in the Village section.The disco (afterhours at the beach bar) was somewhat of a disappointment as it was not very well attended. But you can go there to grab a bite to eat up until 3AM. Staff and entertainmentOverall the staff were very freindly. I never had any problems getting a drink. Sometime I'd go up to the bar and be asked what I wanted by three different bartenders while the fourth was alreadty preparing my order. If you are sitting at a table the waitresses can take some time coming around so I would have to go to the bar to get another drink.( No big deal) The Animation team (entertainment) was very good and they try to keep you entertained. AtmosphereThe week I was there the resort was mostly attended by couples and European tourists (mostly French). Although I did see many different combinations, groups of women , groups of men, some families etc I would definitely go back again.

<Author>MotherVegetable
<Content>Beautiful beach, uneven amenities On the whole, we had a pleasant stay at IFA Bavaro Village. We liked the casual, informal atmosphere. Our room was spacious and clean. Extremely lumpy pillows, erratic a/c, dim lighting (not one but two mystery switches that controlled nothing we could identify), and a balky patio door detracted from the overall comfort of our room. The staff were sweet and good with our kids, the beach and pools were wonderful, and we appreciated the casual buffet-style dining. As for dining here, I can't fairly judge the overall quality of the food, because we are vegetarians and often found it challenging to put together a balanced meal from the offerings. Hot vegetables, pasta, potatoes, and rice dishes were more often than not made with meat (our omniverous companions fared better). The specialty restaurants might have been better, but since we were a large group we opted to stick with the buffets as getting reservations seemed problematic. Wait staff were very nice. Other annoyances: no decaf, few whole grains, vague or misleading signs on the buffet. Beware eating here if you have severe food allergies, unless you speak flawless Spanish! Wonderful fresh fruit, exotic yogurt flavors, and hot chocolate at breakfast, beachside crepes at lunch.Resort wide, there were several issues that we had trouble with. We had asked for two adjoining rooms (small kids involved) but were given rooms across the hall. We were told nothing could be done about this until mid-stay, when the trouble of packing and moving would make it not worthwhile to move. They only give you one room key, regardless of how many occupants of the room. There is also no directory of phone numbers, services, or even a map of the resort; you literally have to blunder around to find things. Our room was close to the beach but also close to one of the bars, and it was pretty loud at night.If you go here, please pledge not to litter on the gorgeous beach. It was heartbreaking to see the discarded cups and straws all over at the end of the day. Pick up after yourself.

<Author>allovertanguy
<Content>We enjoyed the IFA Bavaro Village As many of you know the IFA Bavaro has 3 different resorts within 1. We stayed at the Ocean Village which is the one closest to the beach. Yes, it is also closest to the disco that starts at 11:30- 3:00 A.M. We knew this before and took some ear plugs with us, which we needed. On the plus side, though, we were close to the beach and had one of the buffet restaurants and sports bar right outside our building which was great in the morning for breakfast and later for drinks.The rooms are basic but clean, and as many have indicated the bathrooms need to be redone. Found no bugs in the rooms (we had 2) and always had clean towels. The maid did forget to put water in one of the rooms one day, but we found her and she quickly got more water for us. The food was basic buffet style, but there was always something there that was to our liking. There are three other restaurants as well that you have to make reservations for. We chose the Mexican Restaurant. Basically a mexican buffet. Not very good.We went to the Colonial Restaurant twice and enjoyed it. They had an ala carte menu that had various seafood and meat dishes along with a good selection of appetizers and desserts. We didn't go to the Asian restaurant.The beach of course was great. We would wander down after breakfast and as long as we were there before 9-9:30 we would have no trouble finding a lounge chair. All the chairs were in good shape as they must have been replaced recently. I would say that maybe because it was the holiday season there was not a lot of topless women. Maybe 5% at most at the beach and only a few around the pool.The bars were all good and service was prompt at them all. Our favorite was El Capitan bar. It was great to sit and play some cards after a day at the beach and get a proper drink in a real glass instead of a plastic cup. They also had a cappuccino machine which was nice. They had also recently opened a snack bar at the middle pool which served good pizzas, burgers and hotdogs.While the rooms in this hotel are a little dated most of the other facilities are good and the service was good ,so for what we paid we all agreed that it was good value for the money.

<Author>Falkor
<Content>Great beach, Hotel complex overrated!! Brace yourselves this could be a long one. We just spent the week of dec 31st to jan 7th at the IFA bavaro ocean hotel in D.R. This was my third time to the D.R and my worst experience by far. I have written reviews about all my trips and have been very fair and honest and this will be no exception.We booked through Your Travel tickets.com and they were first class and got the best price. The flights there and back were great with Skyservice. The only snafu was we were not sitting together but within a few minutes of takeoff and a little seat shuffling all was good. On the return we had exit seating which is good because you get an extra foot in front of you.After landing the processing at the aiport was fast and furious and we were on our way. If you are travelling and you don't have a passport yet PLEASE get one as it makes it 100% easier at any port of entry.Arriving at the hotel, first in line for registration, show docs and done quick. I noticed a low room number and that sent up a red flag. I had read through this site that they might try to put you out in the villas upon arrival at night, you being none the wiser. Well they did.The room was something out of a flop house. The bed sagged in the middle, the pillows looked like they were filled with lumpy cotton, the fridge was rusty and didn't close, there were small ants all over the place. Do you get the picture. Off to registration and wow, they were expecting me. Figure that out. they had me on a list already for another room next day at 2 pm. I was not impressed as we were the only couple put in the villas that night.So here we are new years eve and after all the hassle we made it to the party at exactly midnight. Happy new year everyone!!!!The party was awesome with some very impressive fireworks. We met some great people and had a great time. The day after was a little foggy. Get up and off to find a breakfast. After about 10 minutes of going this way and that we find the buffet. CLOSED. we had missed it by 10min. We had no idea as to what times they served as we arrived late and no info is given at registration. So now no food till lunch buffet at 12pm. Go looking for coffee. Only one coffee/cap/expresso machine on resort, another 1/2 hour wait for coffee. Finally its time for the beach, an astounding 15min. walk from the villas. But what a beach! just beautiful,and surprisingly no prob getting chair the first day, but for the most part if you do not put your towels out by 8am you were scavenging for a seat. We watched some seat stealing and even had one of ours taken while on a short walk. Also if you lose your towel you coughed up $20 to replace it. One family of 3 suddenly had 5 towels and this english couple had come back to find their towels had been taken by them, after being ratted on by others they went and took them back and the french lady argued that she needed them for her baby, she went and complained and the english couple were paid a visit and the situation explained with no further problems. 1/2 hour later the woman had 5 towels again and anothe couple had no towels. The saga continued. We spied the beach bar grill and finally had some food. Little did we know it then but they had the best food on the resort and it saved us a few times during out stay. Now its time for our room change and we get one closest to the beach with a ocean view. Maybe a 5min walk. Nice, or so we thought, until we were going to bed and the disco pounded out till 3am. we found if you run the aircond. it drowns out some of the noise, if that makes any sense. My girlfriend still could not sleep and relied on the beach for a few hours each day. We finally settled in and relaxed after day 1 and the week got better.The weather had high 70s to 80s with an offshore wind at about 10 to 20k all week and a few rain showers that were no big deal. Perfect tanning weather. The resort was clean and for the most part the staff very friendly.After the first full round of eating at the buffet we were not impressed. It was the same each day with no themed mealsThank god for the beach grill and the pizza grill it was the best food there and that includes the A'la' cartes. They tried to be food of different countries but missed the mark. The best food we had all week was when we were on a walk and the Melia down the beach had a beach BBQ and we blended in and had lunch with them. LOLThere are no shortage of bars on this resort ...BUT...try to get a drink. They go at a snails pace and if you do not make eye contact or have a tip in your hand you will wait. If you tip the service gets better but if you don't, you wait ..again. We caught on quick and picked a few bars to spread our tips and after a few rounds were instantly recognized, sometimes the drink was poured as they saw me walking up and handed it to me as people still waited for their orders.We quickly found out that as english speaking people we were a definate minority at this resort. The two main languages of the week outside of spanish were Quebec french and german. I am not one to judge other people and their language or culture but wow the majority of the french canadian people were rude and pushy.There were a number of excursions from this resort which we did not do as we have done them before. There were some energetic nighttime shows but after 2 you pretty well saw what they had. The animation staff I feel didn't put in the effort to get people to particpate in activities as they hardly got anyone to particpate. Except for beach volleyball which got pretty competitive.We did meet some fantastic people, Steve and his family from Thunder bay, the principals and thier daughter from T.O and Simon Richard and thier ladies from England. We had some great times, thanx guys! we won't forget you.You kind of get the picture as to how things went. I could probably go on. If you read my other reviews you know we are not the proverbial travel snobs that go and pick out the worst things and trash everything that happens at a resort. These are from the heart opinions.This hotel is a strong 2 1/2 star resort but I feel with a little work it could be a 3 1/2 to 4. It is definately overated.If anyone has any other concerns about this resort that I have forgotten to cover (and I know there has to be something), feel free to contact me via an Email. listed in my profile....Thom  JenniferP.S. did We tell you it has a beautiful beach!!!

The beach.. it was nice. If you want a place to relax without people in youre hair and loud music and people shouting this is not the hotel for you. No matter where you go there is loud music playing there are pelpe walking up and down the beach trying to sell you stuff and they never give up... At one point someone chased us down the beach trying to sell us a pair of earings. It was extremely stressful. As for the weather, it was nice. It only rained during the day once for about 10 minutes and than the sun came up.. it rained almost every night all night. The food was either reallly good or REALLY bad, and i mean really bad. The mexican restaurant was absolutely HORRIBLE. The japanese retaurant was wonderful, we didnt make it to the seafood retaurant. The buffet by the beach was the best... it had the same food everyday for lunch, but it was decent. The ones in the hotel were good... they had plenty of selection for food. In the mornings they had an omlete station and had bacon sausage fruit everything u could want. At night time they had pasta station were you could pick youre sauce youre pasta youre ingredients and so on... Lots of selection but the quality left something to be desired...ALSO... we were pleasantly surprised at our check out when they had told us the day we arrived to be checked out of the room by 4 30.. So we arive at about 4 20 to check out and the guy at the desk tells us we had to be out of the room by noon and that we had to pay a 25 fee because we kept the room for  An extra 4 hours  I would NEVER recomend this hotel to anyone and i would most definetly NEVER return to this hotel.

<Content>Better then Atlantis My fiance and I and another couple stayed at the IFA Bavaro Villas (Ocean Villas) from November 6th - the 13th. Don't let the low cost fool you! This place is worth WAY MORE! This should have a 4-5 star rating!Try the Marinearium tour! It was great!

<Content>Felt like I was camping Just returned from IFA Bavaro Village, Punta Cana.Would never stay there again!!!!! Big yellow stains on the walls, 1 lamp with a shade that looked like it was sat on and put back, bathtub that was so gross I hated taking showers, our toilet did not flush and ants. I swear it is true. Lets talk about the shower... No water pressure at all, and one day we had no hot water. We even had a night without water. Towels, I don't think they know what they are. You were lucky to get a towel by 5 PM. The food was okay. Very hard to get into the specialty resturants, but the buffet was easy to get a seat. The food at the buffet did not change alot, same things everyday. The bar service was very slow, it took a little while to get served and you waited for your order. I was very dissappointed that there was not much to do there. For not being able to leave the compound, they did not offer an activities at night for the guests. They do have a show every night, but that got boring after the second night. The staff was very friendly, and honest. I dropped my wallet, and they returned it to guest services with nothing missing.The resort itself was very nice to look at. They kept that very clean, someone always sweeping, mopping, etc. After talking to several people about the resort, I knew I was not the only person that thought the place was not up to par. I would not recommend this resort to anyone,would never return to the IFA.

<Author>Dwayne&Dixie
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised We booked our trip last minute, and shortly after read the reviews posted on this site, needless to say we were mortified, with the horror stories written by some of the past guests. We decided to go anyway with a little coaxing from my wife and 14 year old son. Our flight was great, we had a short stop over in Puerto Plata, time for a couple Cuba Libre's and back on the plane to Punta Cana. We checked in to our room, which was where I had requested, on the beach, and yes there was a little noise from the beach disco, but after a full day of fun and sun we slept like babies. The rooms were not fancy, but they were clean, the air conditioning worked great. The food we found to be great, breakfast they had omletes, pancakes, fresh friut smoothies, cheeses etc, lunch was a full buffet, and dinner was the same. We, unlike many others, tip a few dollars each time we ate, and a few times at the bar, infact we gave a lot of people working at the hotel a little money, they are very poor!!. Let me tell you that the smile, and service you got there after was excellent and worth every penny. We found most employees friendly, and willing to help, a little spanish also goes a long way, and they appreciate your efforts. The beach was spectacular, the beach cafe was great, chicken wings, pizza, hamburgars, spagettii, fresh fruit etc. There were lots of things to see and do, you could be as busy with trips and sight seeing, or kick back like we did and enjoyed the resort. We did go out the last evening of our trip with one of the beach vendors, Donillo and went to his brothers home and got a real feel for the Dominican people and culture. They are friendly, and very family oriented. It was the best part of our trip, my only wish was that I did it a few days sooner, so we could have spent more time together. To wrap it up I would like to say that we would go back in a heart beat, it was one of the best vacations I have been on in years. We have travelled to Cuba, Mexico, all through the USA, and Canada, so we have some experience with travelling. I'm not sure what people expect from all inclusive resorts that are only making about $50.00 USD per day a person for lodging, food and entertainment, which I forgot to mention was excellent, 10 piece bands, Vegas style performances, costumes, comedy shows etc. We look forward in returning, and will stay for 2 weeks this time, as 1 week wasn't enough. Thankyou to all the people at IFA who worked so hard to show us a good time!!! Muchas Gracias por Todo!!!!! Dwayne, Dixie and Mathew Maul !! Edmonton, Ab. Canada

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great resort for mom  Upon arrival in Punta Cana, got a little nervous that we were the only people getting out at this resort. It was 9:00pm - check in was fast  efficient (about 3 minutes). We were put in the 3000 section of the village which I loved. Overlooking main pool and in the middle of all the action. I would have been disappointed if I was in the villas on the other side. They were old and extremely far from everything. Those people needed a shuttle to get to the main lobby!The staff was fantastic! Bartenders got to know you right away and were always pleasant. Breakfast waiters were terrible but lunch and dinner were wonderful.Beach is the best I've seen and never a problem getting a lounge at either beach or any of the pools.Rooms were clean - two very comfortable double beds for myself and my son. Buffets were good - enought selection so that it wasn't boring. The a la carte restaurants were okay. I would have been upset had it not been included though. Service was not great.Enough to do for my 17 year old son - although the flowing alcohol could be a problem! He met people and there was alot to do for both of us. He liked the disco each night and on the one night when he was later than I'd like - security and front desk were helpful and very compassionate to a frenzied mom!We went on the macao ATV adventure. The sales people were at the hotel every day and since my SUNWING representative was no help whatsoever, I booked the trip. It was shoddy, the vehicles were in disrepair and certainly no safety standards. However; we made the best of it and had a good day. I drove half the way and my son drove half the way.I have stayed at the 4 1/2 star LTI Beach Resort and found this resort to be comparable. I would definitely recommend for someone looking for a smaller resort.

<Author>kujo1695
<Content>Not a bad place, work to be done though Not a bad place to stay for two weeks. It has everything you would expect and is consistent with other 3.5 star resorts. Food is pretty decent and always something at the buffet to suit one's tastes.Rooms we found were clean. Pillows were definitely ready to be replaced so bring your own as I found it difficult to use what they gave us for two weeks. Our bathroom leaked due to the air conditioner condenser as well as a leak under the sink which was fixed after a few days in the room.Staff we found could be a bit rude. I've stayed at other 3.5 star resorts in D.R. and in Cuba and found the service there was superior. This is most likely due to the staff being overworked or something but I found it odd considering the great staff we had in Puerto Plata(same star rating). Ordering a drink at one of the bars could take awhile. The swim up bar isn't actually serviced which is a shame. However, we did find our favourites in the buffets who recognized us quickly and took care of all needs for dinner.Spent most of our day at the beach which is fantastic. Seems to be something everyone agrees with. One is able to do a bit of snorkeling right off the beach area for free (30 US deposit is required though). Careful of the boats as they get close to the swimming area and one actually steered wrong while we were out there and got hung up in the swimmer's area.Entertainment at night is decent. Repeats each week though so we saw some of the same shows twice. The audience involved shows are always good for a laugh.Don't miss the coffee bar El Capitan. Great cappucinnos and coffee to wake you up in the morning. Also, the best prices in gift shops were in the one next to the Villas quiet pool. Saves you from having to haggle with the guys at the beach. One nice thing about the beach is the vendors are all contained in one area so they don't bother you if you don't go to the shop area. Careful of the phony cigars too. We found the guys at the resort cigar shop were great and you may pay a bit more for cigars but it's worth it to know you have the real thing.The disco at the beach at night was good too. Gives you something to do if you feel like staying up a bit late at night.We were disappointed with the security though as a group of students from Spain kept the entire Village section up a few nights all night yelling and screaming under people's rooms and no action was taken by security despite several complaints. Their presence alone likely would have solved this problem.With good weather and good beer it is fairly easy to have a good time here. There is enough to do and we met a lot of great people. However, we found enough small problems added up and there is a way to go before this hotel reaches it's full potential.  
<Date>Apr 30, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>So Much Fun My sister and I, along with 2 girlfriends stayed here March 21-28. We had a wonderful time! I was pretty nervous about going after reading alot of these reviews but once i got there and seen how beautiful everything was my mind was put at ease for the most part. I was terrified to eat EVERYTHING (i tend to be a bit of a picky eater) and so i was scared that i may end up sick. But the food was pretty average. Its a pretty standard spread. I was in desperate need of some protien by day 3 and finally decided to try the chicken...ooooh boy chicken wings never tasted so good! Anyways, all in all the food was fine. Nothing to complain about. THe rooms were always kept very neat and tidy...no complaints there. No bugs. PHEW!! I did however ask to be on the second floor. (less chance of bugs) We had two clean towels every day...if you require more (for hair ect..) i suggest that you bring one from home. THere are NO wash clothes though so you have to bring that if needed! I must add though that sometimes the towels never came until around 5pm and the cleaning ladies will walk right into your room...even if you are in the middle of a shower. They just say hello and are on there way. I found the staff to be quite nice! You must show them respect though if you want it in return....i seen what happens to people who treat them as if they are below them and it is not pretty. The bar by the main pool (with all the activities) takes FOREVER to get a drink, no matter how pleasant you are. Its pretty easy to get a chair for sunbathing in the mornings. I just sugest to be out by 9ish if you want one for sure. There are lots of activities that the staff will try to get you involved with. Its funny at first but by day three of the same thing, you learn to just say no or pretend you are sleeping. haha! We met MANY nice people both young and old and everyone was quite pleasant. This is not really a party resort so if you are just looking to relax then this is the place to be. Now lets talk about the beaches! WOW! BEAUTIFUL!!!! I have never felt or seen sand like that in all my life! And the water is sooooo nice! The beach is certainly something we ALL can agree on! Oh one more thing, if you are needing to email family or friends go to the yellow gift shop (by main pool) it is the cheapest there and the computers run faster there. If you go in between noon and 2 its only a dollar for a half hour. Anyways, I had a great time here with my sister and our friends and i totally suggest staying here. Its a great place for a great price. HAVE FUN!!OH be sure to try the COCO LOCOS mmmmmmmmm......and BANANA MAMMAS........very tasty!  
<Date>Apr 13, 2006

<Author>LaurieAlberta
<Content>Very Beautiful, Relaxing and Clean I just returned from the IFA Bavaro Village yesterday (was there from Mar 21-28). I went with my sister and a couple of girlfriends. My sister and I stayed in the 4100 block of the Ocean Village. Now we are not very high maintenance people, but as with anyone else, we have standards, and i must say that this resort lived up to every one of them. Checking in was a breeze - no problems at all, and they did everything they could to get us all set so that we could go and enjoy the rest of our day. The rooms were perfectly clean - maintained ever single day - even underneath the beds were cleaned, as i had left something under the bed and it was placed on the dresser when i got in later that day. The bathrooms were fine - no leaking bathtubs or ceilings, like many of the reviews i read before going, no bugs anywhere in our room at all. the only complaint i have, and it is a minor one - is that the towel situation is pretty sparse...my sister and i got 2 clean towels every day, which really isnt that bad - but if you require more - bring a couple from home. And you might want to bring faceclothes as well, as there are none of those. The grounds were beautifully maintained - with the walkways, and pool areas being scrubbed every single morning with soap and water. And the grounds themselves were quite pretty just to wander around. The pools were BEAUTIFUL. The most peaceful one is in the Villa section - but if you are looking to participate in daily pool activities - the Village pool is where you want to be. It is also the most crowded, and you do need to get there relatively early - but not at like 6 or 7 in the morning like people have been saying. like by 8:30 or 9. The food was okay - nothing exceptional - but it certainly wasnt as bad as people said either. I could always find something to eat - and my sister - who is extremely picky went away full after every meal as well. The omelettes and banana bread in particular were fabulous. The only minor complaint i had about meal time, was that it was difficult to get drinks - usually had to wait awhile to get them - but that is more due to understaffing than anything else. the servers were incredible - very friendly - and they really appreciate it if you bring them into your vacation, and make them apart of your festivities.....treat them with respect and you will get awesome service. treat them like crap - and that is what you will get. oh, and a couple of drink suggestions - the Coco Locos are fabulous, as are the Banana Mamas - but beware, they can be pretty strong!!!! Now the one thing that most people can agree upon - the BEACH. It truly is amazing. The sand is like baby powder, the water is warm and calm - so great if you are travelling with children, and there arent many vendors to bother you while you are suntanning. There is a market on the beach - so if you want to do your shopping that is where to go. but keep in mind that they ask exorbitant prices - always pay no more than 40% of what they are asking - and it is easier to deal with the men than the ladies....I hope this helps.....it truly was well worth the money - and i think it deserves more than 3.5 stars, and certainly better reviews than a lot of the ones i read......good luck and have fun!  
<Date>Mar 29, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>read this before booking!!! My husband and I just got back on March 7th, we were in the ocean section in the 3400 villa.It was close to the ocean but the noise from the disco every night made for short sleeps. It went until 3AM and the music thumped our room.The new spa they are working on was noisy too.We booked a trip but they never showed up to pick us up..we talked to the liason who books the excursions and he couldnt get ahold of the company that he booked us through, so we were out of luck and then all the other excursions were full so we didnt get to go on anything.The rooms were awful.The bathroom ceiling leaked and every time the upstairs neighbors had a shower our bathroom flooded,the first time it went into my cosmetic bag and ruined my make-up..we complained but nothing was done. The floors were never swept or mopped because my husband dropped a glass and it broke on the first day and there were shards of glass every day for 4 days...I tried to explain to the maid but she didnt speak english so I finally took her broom and cleaned the floor myself.Every single day she left the balcony door unlocked and we were on the first floor..There was a major shortage of towels and we didnt usually get clean ones until 4 or 5 in the afternoon..we wanted a king sized bed and got 2 doubles, we wanted a second floor room and got a first floor room.The rooms smelt really bad, there were dead bugs squished on the walls, some light's didnt work, the tv didnt work for 3 days..There were cockroaches crawling around in the bathroom and in the closet on my clothes..I had to shake them out before I put them on.There were even a few crickets in the bed, I made it a habbit of shaking out the bedding every night.The food made us both sick, so most of the time we had to stay close to the bathrooms. The birds ate the buffet with everyone else.There are ants that bite on the buffet floor.. I started wearing bug spray all the time after the 2nd day, even to sleep in. We didnt find the staff to be very friendly, the pool bar was so slow, we were the only ones at the pool side and had to wait 20 minutes for 2 cokes, the bartenders didnt make any fun drinks but coco loco's, bahama mama's and pina coladas..we thought that we would be able to try lots of fun drinks but nope.We would sit for whole meals without anyone bringing us drinks..even water! The bottles of water in our room were not new when we opend them, but refilled from the water coolers at the bars.Seriously concider staying at another hotel...we are really layed back people and go with the flow but this was really bad.

<Author>Sgt.Dan
<Content>Good value, was impressed, had a great stay My wife, two teenagers, and myself just returned from the IFA Village having stayed there from Mar 5 - 12, 2006. We were in Room 3203 . We were next to the main pool. It was fine, rooms could use an upgrade but air cond was ice cold,food was good with an OK selection. Staff are friendly and polite. Tip the bartenders, they will remember you and look after your beverage needs quickly, or be prepared to stand in line waiting.Entertainment was good. Staff did their best to encourage participation all day long in the many activities they presented. From morning stretching and aerobics to an afternoon of fun activities by the pool, we were happy to be involved. IFA is not a hospital don't just lay around, have fun.Evening entertainment was ok too. They try their best, and can be quite funny. Bingo....Bongo...I was initally worried after reading the reviews on this site, but in spite of some negative reviews, we were quite happy and would return here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Time, Good Bargain I stayed at IFA Bavaro from Feb 4-12. Ill change it up a bit and i wont repeat what everybody else said, The beach is by far the nicest part of the hotel, this isnt a party hotel so anybody looking to have party's this definately isnt the hotel for you, the mini disco is basically for young children, that could either be good or bad, depending if you have young children, there are more retired people then anything tho, the bar is very good during the day time but at night there is big lines, There are not all that many things to do but its All Inclusive so if you sit at the bar you will make the best of your situation, they have internet service there, no mini bar, no tennis courts, and if you can i would try to book it so you are not in one of the town houses that is about 15 min walk to the beach, you actually have to cross a street to get there, but im sure it is quieter, Shopping is very fun, they usualyl give you little freebies for going to there shop, if you are feeling intimidated just keep walking to another shop, people from other stands cannot bother you while you are looking elsewear, soo just keep walking and they will eventually leave you alone, some of the prices are crazy so just pay what you think it is worth and nothing more. Good hotel, good service. but nothing spectacular, good bargain however. 7/10

I would try a different resort because of it. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>ok for the money My husband and I just came back from a long weekend in Punta Cana. I got a great deal on the flight, so I was somewhat desparate to book a hotel 2 weeks in advance pretty much everything was already booked. I found availability in IFA Bavaro and booked it. Yes, I read the reviews, but like I told my husband, I am not going to stay in my room-I am going for the beach and the water. However, this was not the same as I remembered from my last two trips. First and for most, the hotel is HUGE- we were put in the room 20 min walk from the beach. At check in they told us that the next day they had availability closer to the beach, which still turned out a 10 min walk. They have 4 buffet style restaurants, and, as always, breakfast was the best meal of all-can't really ruin eggs. All the food seemed repeat itself every day, needed seasoning, and some of it was just plain nasty tasting. I am one of those people that will try anything, but even I had difficulty varying my diet. All the meat in the buffet are very tough, right from the grill are decent. Smoothies were great-especially pineapple and banana. It was difficult to get coffee served at breakfast-not enough servers with coffee. Drinks were pretty good at all of the bars. The pools were good, but the location of all the lounge chairs was as if were on display to anyone who walked by going to the beach/restaurant. On the beach there were no palapas, which made it difficult to stay in the shade, since the palm trees are very tall. Another thing that really irritated me was that the beach was very noisy and busy with motorized activities. The ocean in Punta Cana as I know it is very quiet and peaceful-no waves, clear waters. Here the motorized boats were very close to the beach all the time, hellicopters flying over, banana boats, just all the time. The rooms were OK, all the necessaties were there. I would not reccomend this hotel if you can afford somthing better.

<Author>mountainman202
<Content>Good deal with very few problems We just got back from 10 days of vacation and it was a good time. (Not a Great Time). This hotel is in the process of some minor renovations. The spa is being built and some needed landscaping on the sidewalks. The resort is divided into 3 zones for rooms. Ocean Rooms, the Village area and the Villas. The ocean rooms are closer to the disco so if you desire some sleep stay in another location because the disco begins at 11:00pm and ends at 3:00am every night. The village rooms are nearer the main pool and the action begins at 10:00am and continues until 5:45pm everyday. The Villas are located at least 15mins walking time from the beach and 5-10mins from the main dining areas.This is the oldest part of the resort and the rooms look like small beach cottages. Kind of run down looking and really far from anything. Our Room= We stayed at the Village and in the 3401 building. Our room faced the main pool and we were on the second floor. Clean and had a balcony overlooking the pool. Very loud all the time because of the constant music and the drunks coming back from the disco at 3:00am every night. The music never changes. The same songs over and over. It's the same routine everyday. Not all rooms face the pool so if you want some peace once in a while take the rooms that face the pond in the back of the building. The room comes with only two large towels and if your lucky a bath mat and a smaller towel. These towels are hard to come by and sometimes after the room was made up we had to go looking for the maid to get even 1 towel. One day we didn't get fresh towels until 6:00pm.We had a power failure at least once a day. No running water lights or A.C. The Food= There were really two areas to eat. One located near the main lobby and the other about half way to the beach. Both are Buffet style and had a good selection of different foods to choose from. They had another buffet type food area on the beach but it was more or less there for lunch and a snack.It doubles as a reservation only for dinner from 7:00pm until maybe 9:30pm then it becomes the disco. On site there are 3 more reservation only restuarants. The Japanese The Carribean and the Mexican. We went to all three and found them to be very good. Our choice of best was the Japanese but if you enjoy a good steak the Carribean was great. (These are included in the all-inclusive program as well.)  The Beach= Nice Nice Nice! But, No palapas, little shade only palm trees and sand. When we arrived there was not enough chairs for everybody so we had to get to the beach before 7:00am to get a seat. About 5 days into our stay they delivered a ton of new chairs so there wasn't a problem after that. Swimming and WaterSports= The swimming area is roped off in two different locations. You can swim about 50 yards out and maybe a 100 yards wide. The water will not be over your head even by the bouys. Kayak and sailing is included but there are no waves at all. plenty of action in the water and safety should be your number one concern. I saw two speed boats driven by tourists go right through the swimming area cutting the ropes and just missing 6 people. No lifeguards. You're on your own! Snorkeling= If you have done snorkeling before you will understand when I say it was AWFUL! No fish no reef off the beach. You can pay for a trip if you want to snorkel or dive. We went on the Soana Island Snorleling trip and saw starfish and some sponges but little fish were present. I've snorkeled in Mexico at Akumel and Cozemel and Grand Cayman. Not even close! Tours and off site= You can get a better deal on the excursions at the Bavaro Plaza in town. Much cheaper than the resort guys. I recommend R.H Tours in Bavaro Plaza next to the sidewalk bar on the corner. No problems at all! Be prepared for culture shock. We took the public transportation(bus). One dollar is the fee and they pick you up at the main road at the bus stop. About a 15 walk from the resort. There is no problem walking to the stop. However once in town you will be hounded by people selling everything. Just say gracias and keep moving. Never pay the asking price for anything ...barter barter and more barter.  Biggest Obstacle= The Language Barrier. Hardly anyone speaks english so be prepared for an adventure if you're not bi-lingual. Not many Americans. Alot of Canadians and French. By far more Germans than anyone else. Staff very friendly but hard to communicate. Overall Rating= This is not a 4 or 5 star resort but a good deal for the money. If I had to rate it from 1-10 I would give this resort a 6 for effort.  
<Date>Feb 28, 2006

<Content>IFA Ocean Village Just OK Just got back from the Ifa Ocean Village Resort Punta CanaBeach was beautiful , weather perfect. <Content>Worst hotel ever... I just came back from a vacation febuary 17th to febuary 24th 2006 at the 1066 room and all I can say is that IFA Villas Bavaro hotel should be rated as a 1 star hotel. In summary: * 20 minutes walk from the polutate beach (algaes are not removed in the morning and used water is thrown in the ocean not too far from the resort), * hundreds of ants in the washroom, 1 lizard on the toilet seat one morning, 1 cockroaches in the bath another one* Bed sheets are not changed once* Only 2 water bottles already unsealed in the room and that's all you get for the week: you must go to the restaurant to get it filled.* the clue of the week: the food was terrible: My sister and I got diarrhia, fever and terrible vomit experience : I am still trying to recover from it. * there was no electricity sometimes for more than 3 hours during the day: the toilet is discusting: no more water to wash your hands: imagine what happend to the food?* The publicity on the resort is lying on the sports activity: there is no Tennis court in the resort: You must walk 20 minutes outside of the resort in the street to get to an abandonned one close to a large garbage dump and ruined houses. * The hotel doesn't offer any water sport: If you want you can deal with an independant boutic at the beach where they ask you minimum 100 US$ deposit each time you want to take the sailing boat or the wind surfing for 1 hour. They don't even let you bring your snorkling. * You must pay a minimum 15$US to take a boat furthur away if you want to snorkle and if you stay at the beach there is no palapa (umbrella from the sun) so you're stuck in the sun without any shade if you spend your day at the beach.* the gym is without electricityIn general I had a good time because I was there with my family! but i was absolutly not well at this resort and I will never go back and I wanted to share my experience with you mostly to reveal the lies under the hotel publicity with regards to sports activity and how sick I got still trying to recover from the fever 3 days after my return.Alexandra - 30 years old Quebec, Canada

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awesome Beaches, Beautiful People and Great Food I just recently returned from a stay at the IFA Bavaro Village Resorts in The Dominican Republic, from Feb.8 to Feb 15, 2006. I tell you I had a great time. First off, once off the plane, you'll take a 20 minute bus ride to the resort. When you arrive, you will be taken to your room and all your luggage will be taken to your room, care of the hotel staff. Remember to give a little tip.. our handler didn't accept the money but we made him take it anyways.. he was happy. Once you get to the room, you will see how clean and well mantained they keep it. The cleaning lady comes in every day in the afternoon to make sure the beds are made and the room is clean..at the end of the trip I gave her a little tip too.. she deserved it. The staff works really hard to make you stay enjoyable and work so many hours.. I don't know were they get there energy! I especially like the animation staff. The second day I was there, I was relaxing at the pool bar and was asked to join a drinking contest.. and suprizingly I won!(I had some tough contenders!!). If your interested, they teach you some Latin dancing and also have stretching exercises that are great. If you like beautiful beaches, this is the place for you. A little warning to some, the ladies do tend to go topless but it didn't bug me at all..LOL! There are also may activities to choose from. At a little extra, we chose to on a 2 hour snorkling excursion. For $65.00US, you get your own little speed boat and get to go out to see some beautiful coral and sea fish of all kinds. Back at the resort, you have great nightly entertainment at the entertainment pavillion, which starts around 10p.m. If you arrive there early, the staff is more than willing to ask you to dance on the stage before the show. After the show, if you still have the energy, you can walk or take the mini bus(which runs practically all day and night), to the disco. We decided one night, to take a 15 to 20 minute taxi ride to a dance club called Mangu. Its a great place to hang out with the locals. A reminder though, you are leaving the resort, so bring some extra cash if you want to drink..beers usually cost around $3.00US. We ended up staying there until 5 or 6a.m. It's also a good idea to go with a willing hotel staff member or someone that knows at least some basic Spanish. We found that the breakfast, lunch and dinner buffets really good. Another great thing they have is a snack bar, which runs all day until 2a.m. There, you can have rice, fries, pizza, hot dogs, hamburgers, and my favourite, fried chicken. They also provide 7 a la carte meals, which you can make reservations for at he front lobby. My favourite was the Mexican restaurant called Jalisco. We also tried Japanese and Carribean food at a place called Carribe. If you like lobster, spend $30.00US and treat yourself, it to die for! If you want to shop, there are tons of shops beside the resort. But remember to talk the price down or just walk away, they'll come running for you for your business.. I personally talked the guy down from $75.00 purchase to like $25.00purchase! Overall the trip was excellent, and I strongly recommend going here!! Remember to bring a camera to capture the memories, because I know that I had so many.. HAVE FUN!!  
<Date>Feb 20, 2006

<Content>simply wonderfull Punta Cana, IFA Bavaro Ocean VillageTrip advisor member from Montreal , CanadaFebruary 13, 2006We arrived last night after 8 fantastic days !!! About the weather...Alwyas a cloudy sky soon in the morning but a shiny sky for the rest of the day (always over 30 degrees)!!! About the beach....If you want to walk in white and soft sand, this is THE PLACE to. The temperature of the water was around 30 degrees. Food is good. People are very friendly. On the site, you have many restaurants, pools, gift shops, bars and also a pharmacy and a playground for your children. All meals and beverages (included drinks, beer and wine) are included in the price of your trip....I strongly recommend this place and if I have a chance, I will return over there !!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not bad, but I would go elsewhere. My wife and I stayed at the IFA Villa Bavaro from January 6-13. I am 31 and she is 27 years old, and we are from the Detroit area. We stayed in the villas located the farthest from the beach. The rooms are kinda beat up but do the job. There is a mini-fridge, but it only has 2 1 liter bottles of water that do not get restocked unless you tip the housekeeper about $5 a day. $3 a day was not cutting it. :D The room also had no map of the resort and other such literature you usually find. The televisions also have no remote. The a/c was ice cold though which was a bonus. I ran across no bugs at all, which can be common in first floor rooms.It is a LONG walk to the beach from the Villa rooms. There are also other traditional 2 story buildings closer to the water that do not look and feel like cabins up north. The bars have El Presidente' beer which is excellent. The rum is from the tap but it tasted great. I saw no drink menus for the foo-foo drinks that the girls like. I think they can make them all, but a menu would be nice. The bartenders were friendly like most places. The buffet was not that great. I am not a picky eater either. I eat everything. The food was just decent, and the selection was small. I have been to many other Dominican hotels that have 3 times the buffet.I like to wander to the snack bar late at night after drinking all day, but the only snack bar they have is located on the beach. It took about 15 minutes or brisk walking to get there from our room. Obviously you return to the room sweating with cold food. :(I have been to the Dominican Republic at least 5-6 times before and this place was the worst. Not horrible, but I would recommend going to another resort. I also think they had a sale for this resort at a European trailer park. I have never seen so many people pick their noses in the buffet line, spitting phlegm globs on the pool deck, or being just generally rude. Americans love to complain about euro-rudeness, but I have never seen it like this before. The beach was nice but need more chairs. There was a ton of empty sand. They also rope off the swimming area. It is tiny. I usually bring my own snorkel and fins and go out by my self from shore. They will not let you do this. You would be happy here if you have never been anywhere else. I had a good time, but I will go elsewhere next year.

<Author>Whomiam
<Content>A great place to visit... for a week. Flight: We flew to Punta Cana with Transat Airlines. We were served a rather tasty meal, the movies were reasonably current and there was a pillow and blanket for every passenger. The only complaint would be that in 7 hours of flying they only served drinks twice (ie:2 cups of fluids in 7 hours). We were dehydrated by the time we arrived. Hotel: The hotel was reasonable for a 3 star. I wouldn鈥檛 expect much more 鈥?or be happy with much less. The rooms were basically clean except that the walls didn鈥檛 appear to have been washed in a while (the remains of squashed bugs were still stuck to the walls and ceiling). The room had full width patio doors which let lots of light. The downside is that our particular room backed on to a grey-water lagoon which had an unpleasant smell at times (the 3500 block, avoid it). So we didn鈥檛 use the patio or keep the doors open as much as we would like to have. Pools/beach:The pools and beach were excellent. The beach has the softest sand we have touched鈥?and we have been around the world. We never had to fight for chairs but that was because we were usually ahead of the crowd. I imagine anyone who came mid-afternoon might have trouble finding an empty one. There is a beachside bar and grill for mid-day drinks and meals. To get to the beach we walked 100m to the end of the hotel, another 50m through a sandy, well treed area and then maybe another 20m to the water. There are much closer rooms but the closest ones are close to the disco and hence, are more noisy at night (so we have been told). Somewhere in between might be a good compromise. Drinks: Drinks were served fairly strong 鈥?much stronger than Mexican resorts and a bit stronger than North American standards. Rhonda ordered hers with 鈥減oco鈥?alcohol. I was impressed that they served the best quality Bavaro rum made on the island if you ordered it on the rocks. It was smooooth鈥?like drinking good scotch with a rum flavour. It became Dale鈥檚 favourite and he bought two bottle of the rum to take home. Excursions: As far as tours go, we hit the jackpot. Based on another review here at this site we contacted Wim Goessens --------. There were six of us travelling together and he took us on 2 personal tours (we had 8 on the second as we invited another couple we had met). Each was a full day (8 AM to 6 or 7 PM). Wim鈥檚 tours allow you to 鈥渆xperience鈥?the country as opposed to just seeing it. Where the Jungle Safari takes you to a school that has been set up to accommodate tours, Wim takes you a remote school where the children don鈥檛 see many visitors. I鈥檒l tell you鈥?DR kids are not well behaved. We visited the home a several real REAL DR families, not actors paid to entertain tourists; and we experienced two home cooked typical Dominican lunches (except that Wim made them include vegetables, which are not a part of a regular DR diet). We fell in love some of the children. Knowing what I now know about what happens to girls when the become 鈥渙f age鈥?I wished I could adopt the daughter of one of these families 鈥?she was so bright and could have a great future 鈥?if she was given half a chance. It won鈥檛 happen in DR. Win took us snorkelling to a less used site (albeit, the coral was noting compared to other places), swimming in a local river (some local kids joined us鈥?we taught them how to skip rocks and they caught a tarantula for us to see), to a natural grotto (where it looked like we were about to be robbed until Wim pulled his gun out of his pocket and tucked it into his belt where it could be seen) and to a beach where the waves are much bigger and we could go body surfing. We also visited a waterfall (rare in this part of the island) and walked down the creek for a so called 鈥渏ungle walk鈥?(more arid than jungle, nothing like central or South America). Wim鈥檚 stories are very interesting, It was such an eye opener. He has been on the island for 10 years, most of which was as a manager at one of the resorts. He knows how the resorts work. He was also one of those so called 鈥渉osts鈥?for one of the airlines at one time. What a scam. They are sales people there to sell tours, not provide service. They get HUGE commission and send you with a local tour company contracted to them (the tour company only get 50% of what you pay). These same local companies aren鈥檛 allowed to take you directly as a client but there are other local companies or guides (like Wim) who can. These are more personalized tours and charge less ($300 for the six on us on the first tour, 20% less on the second). The sales people (oops, I meant hosts/hostesses) will discourage you from booking with these local companies for obvious financial reasons. The only complaint about Wims鈥?tour was that when we paid him in peso鈥檚 at the end he ripped us off on the exchange rate 鈥?getting ripped off is a true Dominican experience. Food: The best food by far was at the Caribe restaurant (poor service, but great food). The DR restaurant was a close 2nd (make sure you order the rice pudding) and the Beach Grill 3rd (best service overall, but not a great menu). We didn鈥檛 like any of the 6 dishes we ordered at the Mexican and the buffet tended to be mostly bland food 鈥?although they would sometimes have something good frying on the grill. Dysentery: There are a number of reasons why people get sick at all-inclusive resorts like this. 1) The weather is hot and we can easily become dehydrated. 2) The food is rich 鈥?our stomachs aren鈥檛 used to rich foods day-in and day-out for a week. 3) Alcoholic drinks are free 鈥?we end up drinking far more alcohol than we are used to. 4) Some of the drinks contain coconut milk (eg Pina Collata) 鈥?a natural laxative. 5) We are not accustomed to drinking 鈥渨ater鈥?(as opposed to other fluids) and our body needs water to flush out all the junk we have been eating/drinking. 6) Warmer temperatures grow bacteria faster 鈥?it is near impossible to avoid some contact with it. Hence, drink LOTS of bottled water, use some restraint with rich foods and be prepared to have some discomfort at one point or another. It is part of the price you pay.

<Author>ontcanuck
<Content>Fantastic We arrived at the IFA lobby Jan. 29 at 10:00 pm to a warm reception. Although we were booked for the Villas we were given a room in the Ocean section 4100 but after 1 night we were kept awake by the disco on the beach. The next day we told the front desk,our problem they went out of their way to get us a better room and to our surprise we were given a room in the village section on the 2nd floor over looking the pool.The resort is divided into 3 sections, the farthest part of the resort is the Villas which is 1.36 km.(16min.) walk to the water on the beach.The villas are beautifull and charming cottage style buildings with well lit sidewalks. In the Villas there is avery large pool and a bar. In the same area there is a large stage that has nightly entertainment (9:30 to 11:00)also there are 3 ala carts mexican, dominican and caribe (reserve at the main lobby at 9:00 am.), 2 of them are turned into a breakfast buffet in the morning. A little further in the Villas there is a Coffee Bar and a lounge area, they also serve alcohol.You then continue across a small parking lot where you come to the main lobby, this is where the village section starts. Here there is another large pool , a swim up bar and a very large Buffet (Calibri) . There are 6 buildings surrounding the pool 3100 to 3600 these probably are the nicest rooms location wise and this is where a lot of the action is.Next comes the Ocean section 4100 to 4600 closest to the beach. Here there is a smaller pool with a bar and another large Buffet (La Casona) where they serve ice cream at lunch.Then comes the beach which is packed all day so get your chairs early. There is a lot of shade here and also open areas. The bar here is part of a lunch area (12:30 to 4:00)and a ala cart at night(booked here at 12:30), also serves as a disco from 11:00 pm. to 2:00 am. This the only place you can get hot dogs and pizza.This resort should be rated a lot better almost a 5 star.FOOD: execelent and lots of choicePOOLS: fantastic, towels always availableENTERTAINMENT: these are the hardest working people in the resort and their shows are fantastic.ROOMS: all rooms were very nice, up to date and freshly painted. There are also small fridges in the rooms stocked daily with bottled water.GROUNDS: beautifull with flowers everywhere.EXCURSIONS: we went on 2. Monster truck safari- OK but not great, the trucks were so noisy you could not hear the tour guide and people were packed like sardines about 30 to a truck. Done the outback safari and it's much better. we talked to some people who took a outback trip with a small operater Wim Goesen and a very small group . It was a lot cheaper and more personal.2nd excursion was the Bavaro Trackers (ATVs) it was a blast.There is also a Grand Prix go cart track( the carts are very fast) 10 min. from the resort run by a German. He will pick you up at your resort and take you back free.Have the hotel or tour operater call them for a pick the brochures are at the front desk. warning they only take cash.My only complaints are no orange juice,no kleenex or wash cloths in the rooms and the pizzas are awfull.I hope this helps and if you want to know anything else feel free to e-mail me. PS: did not see 1 mosquito anywhere

<Content>It's a 3rd world country people!! The biggest problem is why is it people (99% Americans) just don't get it! It's a 3rd world country people! Yes, there are bugs, yes it rains, yes the language is different, yes the food is not american, yes plumbing and water pressure differ than home, yes you might get sand in your pants... serious folks what where you expecting?? 99% of us probably spent less than a weeks pay for flight, room, 24/7 food, booze, sun and sand - so in all honesty you will always get MORE than you paid for!As for the hotel - wonderful. <Author>HappyWanderer
<Content>o.k. for adults December 2004 We visited Punta Cana Dec 2-9 and our party consisted of my husband and I (40's) and our 4 boys ages 14,11,9,5. I found your site so helpful, I was compelled to send in our review. The airport experience coming and going was excellent. We moved through efficiently and were shuttled to our hotel about 20 min. away. They did have us in a line to have our pictures taken, but the line moved very quickly and did not slow us down at all. On the return trip, we were brought to the airport far too soon and had to spend 3 hours waiting around. It would have been better to stay at the resort a bit longer. The resort is divided into 3 areas:Villas, Village and Ocean. It is hard to determine where the Village and Ocean separate because it all runs together, but the Villas are separated by a road. Although there are 3 lobbies all areas use the Village lobby for check in. The Villa's were numbered in the 1000's and had the smallest rooms. They would be the quietest location. The Village/Ocean rooms were 3000's and 4000's and that is where most of the activity is. While we were there, the Villas were unoccupied until the last 2 days. The pool and bar area were open, and they have a coffee bar in their 'lobby'. The pool at the Villas was the biggest and quietest and the Ocean was the smallest but offered the most shade. We spent most of our pool time at the Villas. There was a nesting duck sitting on her eggs under the stairs leading to the bar and it fascinated my 2 younger boys. All the grounds were lovely and well kept up and we found it a nice stroll from one end to the beach. If your room is in the far end of the Villa's (high 1000's) it would be a very long walk to the beach (close to 2 km?). There is a shuttle the runs from the Village lobby to the Ocean lobby and then to the beach. The patrons were mostly Europeans - French, Italian, Germans, followed by Canadians and very few Americans. I would recommend learning a few Spanish phrases because not all the staff spoke English. We found the D.R.people to be very friendly and willing to try and communicate. Between our limited Spanish, their broken English and hand gesture we made out O.K.  Our check in was fine. They put us in 2 rooms but they were not adjoining, so we were moved the next day. We went from the 3700 block to the 4100 block. Both rooms were similar with air conditioning, mini-bar, bath/shower, TV. , balcony. The beds are hard and some of the foam was breaking down in the pillows. If you are fussy you should bring your own pillow. It would be handy on the airplane as well. The animacion team worked hard. They started at 10:00 with dancing lessons, volleyball, aerobics etc. and worked throughout the day. The nightly entertainment was pretty sad, but we noticed an improvement the last 2 nights. I'm not sure if it was because they were getting ready for the Xmas influx or because of the Urology convention that arrived, but the venue was moved from the village area to the villas and it did get better, as did the food. Speaking of food...My motto is if I don't have to cook it, it's good, but truthfully the food was so-so. There were 2 buffets, a seafood a la carte restaurant and a beach grill that became an a la carte restaurant in the evening and later the same restaurant became the disco. The fresh fruit was plentiful as were the salads, but most of the buffet items tasted the same. The beach grill was the best. They grilled various meats in front of you (beef steak - very tender, pork chops, chicken, hamburgers). They also served hot dogs and pizza. The buffet closest to the beach had an ice cream dispenser which was also a hit with the kids. This buffet usually had little hamburgers at lunch and the other buffet had a pasta bar every evening. The Kids Club was the worst part of the resort. It was a sad little building with an even sadder looking girl. I'm not sure what languages she spoke but English was not one. My son went one day and lasted 20 min. There was one other child there and he was also Canadian and they played a board game. That was the only day we noticed anyone attend. I had expected scheduled events that my children could choose to participate in, but this was more of a babysitting service. If they offer a Kids Club, they should run it properly, otherwise they should not mis-lead the patrons. The beach was huge. Most hotels sit very close to the waterfront, but this resort is set back several hundred meters. You can walk on the sand to get to the water, walk on a paved path or take the shuttle. The sand is powdery soft and fine. There is no shortage of beach chairs, but shade is hard to find. My boys all wore water shirts and we did not have any problems with sunburns. The wind coming off the ocean was very strong, so although we wanted to spend our time at the beach, the gale-force winds moved us to the pools each day. We looked into some of the tours, but the cost for a family of 6 held us back. We found a man on the beach that took us snorkeling in his motorboat for 1/3 of the cost offered by the tour companies. The current was very strong and the waves can get quite high. We also took a cab into the closest town for some shopping and preferred that to the beach vendors set up beside the hotel. We found one store run by 3 girls and they were so relaxed. They offered the lowest prices and they didn't haggle like most places. We bought coffee for $3/lb as well as some trinkets. Everytime we bought something they would give us a necklace. The vendors at the beach can get very aggressive. Some things we brought or should have brought: Lots of sunscreen and medications you might need ( bug spray with Deet, Solarcane, Reactine, Advil) You might not need them, but it is very expensive to buy there. Insulated travel mugs are a great for the beach and leave them with the bartenders when you go home. They really appreciate it. Inflatable mattresses. Footballs or some activities for the kids. Our boys spent a lot of time tossing a little football around. Bring around $50. in U.S. $1. bills. We tipped the maids, bartenders and waiters. It did not seem to be the usual practice at the resort and it did not change the service, but the wages are so low we felt better doing it. We also brought little gifts for the maids (lipsticks, hair accessories, candies etc.) as well as toys and coloring books for children. We did not make it to the country, so we left most of the stuff with the maids. Lastly, 4 out of 6 of us got sick with a stomach upset, but not at the same time. We cannot determine if it was the water, ice, food or if it was a bug we brought with us from home. It kept 2 of them in bed for close to 2 days, so thankfully they have American T.V. stations. We took 3 of our boys to Riviera Maya 2 years ago and they much preferred Mexico to D.R. They liked to go Boogey Boarding which they couldn't do at Punta Cana. The water was very calm in the D.R., but the strong winds kept us from enjoying the beach. The snorkeling was also much better in Mexico. It was a high-end resort and the staff was fluent in English, so I'm sure that influenced their preference. Would we return to the D.R.? I would hesitate to go to a resort less than 4 or 5 stars because of the amenities they provide for the children. If the trip was for my husband and me, it would have been fine. We would have gone for long walks, explored more and socialized with other couples, but having the children with us, we found the resort limited. I'm sure a 5* resort would have had better evening shows, better kids club, more youth activities and better food variety, and with the ages of our children that would have taken our experience from so-so to terrific.  
<Date>Dec 15, 2004

<Author>theoldboot65
<Content>Barcelo Bavaro Village, a good little inexpensive place to hang your hat ! A little late on writing this review but considering what I went through this year, in Puerto Plata at the Bahia Principe San Juan, I figured I had better give the kudos where they are deserved.This little 3+ star resort far, far outweighed the 4+SUP Bahia Principe by a tonne! What I will do is compare the Barcelo with the Bahia so EVERYONE will be forewarned NOT to go to Puerto Plata (or at least to the Bahia Principe)While we vacationed at the Barcelo Bavaro village, we had a great time, the rooms, as is stated in other reviews are a little dated and maybe need some freshening up, but hey, the beds are clean, the bathroom is clean, what more do you need. We had no roaches or ants while at the Barcelo Bavaro; I tipped the maid a buck a day and took little things from the dollar stores as little gifts, such as Crayola pencil crayons for her children, little flash lights, nail polishes/lip glosses, etc. and at the end of the trip, I gave her alot of the girls summer clothes 'cause they won't be fittin' them next year, therefore she could use them and she really appreciated it, clean towels and all every day.Now, while at the Bahia, the first impression is WOW, until you get to your room, which happened to be in the back of the property, near the dumpsters, and the sewage collection, the rooms sucked, no door sweeps on the bottoms, therefore, bugs, and I do NOT mean one or two, I mean literally, an infestation of HUNDREDS of creepy crawling millipedes, on the walls, the drapes, the floors, and brace yourself, the beds! Of course we immediately requested a room change, and were told that oh most certainly we could move, but for 30$ US per night! Well, I don't think so! I am totally serious about the wormy creepers in the beds too--I complained BIG TIME, showed the maid, and the manager and they laughed at me because they thought I was afraid of these little bugs, their solution, i got a can of insecticide that I was to spray, really good for growing girls to inhale.Food at the Barcelo Bavaro (BB) was good, every nite was a themed evening, one night mexican, the next perhaps, chinese, and so on, it was truly edible and always fresh and hot, with tons of variety.At the Bahia Principe (BP), the food buffet was the same each and every night with the exception of a few different dishes thrown in. the food was tasteless, cold and just plain BLAH---and if you are a bacon lover, there is NO bacon at the BP in the morning, we were there for a week and not one slice of bacon was seen.The beach at the BB was beautiful, absolutely pristine white sand with the aquamarine coloured ocean--breathtaking (did get a few little bites from teh sand fleas) but was prepared for that from reading the reviews.OK, the BP--the beach consists of hotel employees filling up huge cloth bags with the gritty thick brown sand and lying them side by side, as the tide washes the beach away, one day we walked the entire beach and it was flat, the next morning we walked it again and half the beach was gone, it had been washed away, so these guys literally build the beach back up daily, the water was horrid while we were there, it was quite wavy and therefore the water itself had been churned up and was brown and filthy with sand bits. In neither place did we spend alot of time on the beach, for the simple reason of the fleas, you do get alot of bites and they itch like mad.Drinks BB beer was okay, a little watery but so is every thing else. You can flash a buck at the bartender and he will whip you up whatever you want fresh and forego the slushie machine drinks.Over at the BP, the drinks are much the same, they are slushie machine drinks, spinning with ice all day, so they too are quite watery, same rule applies tip a buck and you won't be sorry.Staff at the BB, are friendly and accomodating, to us they provided every thing we requested and were quick to do so. As were the maids, bartenders everyone.Now the BP, like I said, they laughed at us for being afraid of the crawling worms in our rooms, they wouldn't move us only for a charge. No service at the pools. Waiters make strange meowing noises at our rather good looking daughters--did not go over well with DAD! Not accomodating what so ever, they do not speak english (or at least they didn't to me) and make like they don't understand what you are saying. There were tons of Europeans at this resort, and some of them are very friendly while others are quite bold, butting into lines etc. I suppose that happens all over at this type of place, just sit back let them go first then get in line when the feeding frenzy is near being done.All in all, i would most certainly go back to the BB in a split second, the BP will never go back there as long as I live, and this place was recommended to me by the Travel agent, she apparently had been there! I asked her if she was on glue when she was there or something, man it was a horrible spot, but of course--ya got your kids there so you have to make the most of it for them and I suppose you are off work for the week and there are no dishes or laundry to be done--Puerto plata was the grungiest place I had every seen, Punta Cana is cleaner and less populated.Hope this helps, as for the (BP) JUST DONT DO IT! You know how when the bus comes to pick you up to take you to the airport, most of us sorta feel like oh this is it, and sort of loiter around the bus, well at the BP people were actually fighting to get on the bus to get outta there ASAP--honestly it was that bad!!!
